Salah — Prayer
beginner
5 min
Ruling on Ta'awwudh Before Recitation
Specifies who recites ta'awwudh and its timing in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who recites ta'awwudh in prayer and explain the Hanafi position that it is sunnah and dependent on qira'ah.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah for those who recite, not for the muqtadi.

In this passage, the author specifies the ruling of ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) before recitation in prayer. The text clarifies that ta'awwudh is not for everyone; it is only for those who will recite the Quran. This includes the imam, the munfarid, and the masbuq, but excludes the muqtadi. The proof is derived from the Quranic command and the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage is about ta'awwudh and its ruling level. The text states that ta'awwudh is recited silently by those who will recite the Quran.
The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Determine who recites ta'awwudh
From the text, identify that the imam, munfarid, and masbuq recite ta'awwudh, but the muqtadi does not. Note the reason: only those who perform qira'ah recite it.
Muqtadi does not recite qira'ah in Hanafi.
3
Locate the dalil
The text cites Quran 16:98 and a hadith from Abu Dawood as proofs. The Quranic command 'fa'ista'idh' links ta'awwudh to recitation.
The hadith shows the Prophet's practice of ta'awwudh before recitation.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse uses the conditional 'when you recite', indicating that ta'awwudh is tied to the act of recitation, not to the prayer itself.
Hence, those who do not recite are not commanded.
5
Note the practical consequence
In a congregation, the muqtadi remains silent during the imam's audible recitation and does not recite ta'awwudh. The masbuq recites it when he completes his missed rak'ahs.
This is a key distinctive feature of Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستفتح كل مصل (٤٥٧) ثم يتعوّذ سرًا للقراءة فيأتى به المسبوق لا المقتدى ويؤخّر عن تكبيرات العيدين (٤٥٨) ثم يسمّى سرّا ويسمّى في كل ركعة قبل الفاتحة فقط ثم قرأ الفاتحة
تشریح : پھر آہستہ سے اعوذ باللہ من الشیطان الرجیم ، پڑھے ، جن لوگوں کو قرآت کرنی ہے وہی اعوذ باللہ پڑھے گا، اور جن کو قرآت نہیں کرنی ہے وہ اعوذ باللہ اور بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھے ۔ چنانچہ مسبوق بعد میں قرآت کرے گا اس لئے وہ اس وقت اعوذ باللہ، اور بسم اللہ پڑھے گا۔ عیدین کی تکبیرات زوائد کے بعد قرآت پڑھے گا اس لئے تکبیرات زوائد کے بعد اعوذ باللہ، اور بسم اللہ پڑھے گا۔ اور مقتدی چونکہ قرآت نہیں کرے گا اس لئے وہ اعوذ باللہ ، اور بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھے گا۔ وجه : (١) آیت یہ ہے۔ فاذا قرأت القرآن فاستعذ بالله من الشيطان الرجیم - ( آیت ، ٩٨ سورۃ النحل (١٦) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرآت قرآن سے پہلے اعوذ باللہ الخ پڑھے۔ آیت سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اعوذ باللہ قرآت کے تابع ہے، ثناء کے تابع نہیں ہے (٢) ۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدری قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قام من الليل كبر ..... ثم يقول : الله اكبر كبيراً ثلاثا ، اعوذ بالله السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم من همزه و ن و نفشه ثم يقرأ. ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب من رأی الاستفتاح بسجانک ص ١٢١ نمبر ٧٧٥) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اعوذ باللہ کے بعد قرأت کرے اس لئے یہ قرآت کے تابع ہے۔
ترجمه (٤٥٨) پھر آہستہ سے "بسم اللہ" پڑھے اور ہر رکعت میں صرف فاتحہ سے پہلے بسم اللہ پڑھے۔ پھر فاتحہ پڑھے تشریح اعوذ باللہ کے بعد بسم اللہ ، پڑھے ، پھر سوہ فاتحہ پڑھے ، جسکو فاتحہ پڑھنا ہو وہی بسم اللہ پڑھے، چنانچہ حنفیہ کے یہاں مقتدی فاتحہ نہیں پڑھے گا تو وہ بسم اللہ بھی نہ پڑھے گا۔۔ صرف فاتحہ سے پہلے کہہ کر یہ بھی بتانا چاہتے ہیں کہ سورت سے پہلے بسم اللہ نہ
Every worshiper opens with (the thana) (457) then he seeks refuge (ta'awwudh) silently for the recitation, so the masbuq (latecomer) recites it, not the muqtadi (follower), and it is delayed after the extra takbirs of the two 'Eids. (458) Then he says 'Bismillah' silently and says it in every rak'ah only before al-Fatihah, then he recites al-Fatihah.
Explanation: Then silently recite 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'. Those who have to recite (qira'ah) will recite 'A'udhu', and those who do not have to recite will not recite 'A'udhu' or 'Bismillah'. Thus, the masbuq will recite later, so he will recite 'A'udhu' and 'Bismillah' at that time. In the 'Eid prayer, after the extra takbirs, he will recite qira'ah, so after the extra takbirs he will recite 'A'udhu' and 'Bismillah'. As for the muqtadi, since he does not recite qira'ah, he will not recite 'A'udhu' or 'Bismillah'. Proof: (1) The verse: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge in Allah from the accursed Satan.' (An-Nahl 16:98) From this verse it is understood that before reciting the Quran, one should say 'A'udhu billah'. Also from the verse it is understood that 'A'udhu' is dependent on qira'ah, not on thana. (2) In the hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: 'When the Messenger of Allah would stand at night, he said the takbir... then he said: Allahu akbar kabiran three times, A'udhu billah al-Sami' al-'Alim min al-shaytan al-rajim min hamzihi wa nafkhihi, then he would recite.' (Abu Dawood, chapter on those who saw opening with Subhanak, p.121, no.775) In this hadith, he recited after 'A'udhu', so it is dependent on qira'ah.
(458) Then silently recite 'Bismillah' and recite it in every rak'ah only before al-Fatihah. Then recite al-Fatihah. Explanation: After 'A'udhu', recite 'Bismillah', then recite Surah al-Fatihah. Those who have to recite al-Fatihah will recite 'Bismillah'. Hence, according to the Hanafis, the muqtadi does not recite al-Fatihah, so he will not recite 'Bismillah' either. By saying 'only before al-Fatihah', he also wants to indicate that before a surah, one does not recite 'Bismillah' (in prayer).
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) and basmalah (saying 'Bismillah') before recitation in prayer. It is a ruling_with_proof type. The matn (457) states that after the thana, the worshiper recites ta'awwudh silently, but only those who will recite qira'ah do so. The masbuq (one who joined late) recites it because he will recite later, while the muqtadi (follower) does not, as he does not recite. In 'Eid prayer, the ta'awwudh is delayed until after the extra takbirs. (458) states that basmalah is recited silently before al-Fatihah in every rak'ah. The commentary explains the logic: ta'awwudh is dependent on qira'ah. The proof from Quran (16:98) commands isti'adha before recitation, and the hadith of Abu Sa'id shows the Prophet doing so after takbir and before reciting. For basmalah, the Hanafi position is that it is recited silently before al-Fatihah, not before other surahs in prayer, and the muqtadi does not recite it because he does not recite al-Fatihah. This is based on the principle that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower in audibly recited prayers.

Key Terms
تعويذ (ta'awwudh): The act of seeking refuge with Allah from Satan; the phrase 'A'udhu billah...'.
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregation late and misses part of the prayer with the imam.
مقتدي (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, who recites ta'awwudh (A'udhu billah) before recitation in prayer?
A) The imam only
B) The muqtadi (follower) only
C) Anyone who will recite qira'ah (imam, munfarid, masbuq), not the muqtadi
D) Every worshiper including the muqtadi

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh in prayer is sunnah for anyone who recites Quran, and is not recited by the muqtadi.

Ruling on Basmalah Before Al-Fatihah
Explains the Hanafi ruling on basmalah recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on basmalah in prayer and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Basmalah is recited silently before al-Fatihah in every rak'ah, and is not recited by the muqtadi.

This passage continues with the ruling on basmalah. The author instructs that after ta'awwudh, the worshiper says 'Bismillah' silently, and only before al-Fatihah. The muqtadi does not recite basmalah because he does not recite al-Fatihah. This is a distinctive Hanafi position, differing from the Shafi'i school where basmalah is considered part of al-Fatihah and recited aloud in audible prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that basmalah is recited silently after ta'awwudh. It is a sunnah, not wajib.
The ruling level for basmalah in prayer is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Determine when and where basmalah is recited
The text specifies 'in every rak'ah only before al-Fatihah'. This means it is not recited before other surahs in prayer.
This is unique to prayer; outside prayer, basmalah is recited before every surah.
3
Identify who recites basmalah
Following the same principle as ta'awwudh, only those who recite al-Fatihah recite basmalah. Thus, the muqtadi does not recite it.
The muqtadi's recitation is replaced by the imam's in audible prayers.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that basmalah is part of al-Fatihah and is recited aloud in audible prayers. The Hanafi school considers it separate and recited silently.
This is a well-known ikhtilaf between the two schools.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
In a Hanafi congregation, the imam recites basmalah silently before al-Fatihah. The muqtadi does not recite it. The masbuq recites it when he completes his missed rak'ahs.
This ensures consistency with the principle that the follower does not recite.

Source Text

( ابوداؤد شریف، باب من رأی الاستفتاح بسجانک ص ١٢١ نمبر ٧٧٥) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اعوذ باللہ کے بعد قرأت کرے اس لئے یہ قرآت کے تابع ہے۔

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) and basmalah (saying 'Bismillah') before recitation in prayer. It is a ruling_with_proof type. The matn (457) states that after the thana, the worshiper recites ta'awwudh silently, but only those who will recite qira'ah do so. The commentary explains the logic: ta'awwudh is dependent on qira'ah. Key Terms
بسم الله (basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' recited before al-Fatihah in prayer.
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregation late and misses part of the prayer with the imam.
مقتدي (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind the imam.

The Opening Supplication in Salah: Sunnah for All
Explanation of the opening supplication after takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the opening supplication (istiftah) in the Hanafi school, identify its proof from the hadith, and explain why it is recited by both imam and follower.

Core Idea
The opening supplication is sunnah for every person in salah, because it is not qira’ah.

After the opening takbir, every person praying—imam and follower alike—recites a brief supplication before seeking refuge and reciting the Fatiha. This lesson examines the ruling of this opening supplication, its evidence from the Sunnah, and the Hanafi position that the follower recites it, unlike the Fatiha which the imam carries on behalf of the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the opening supplication is and what legal category (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.) the Hanafi school assigns to it.
The text says 'every praying person opens' indicating generality.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the specific hadith cited as proof and note its source (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud).
The hadith is from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri describing the Prophet's night prayer.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The phrase 'kana yaqul' indicates habitual practice, which in Hanafi usul signals recommendation (sunnah) rather than obligation.
The hadith does not command; it describes consistent practice.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Compare with the Shafi'i position: they prefer a different wording and may restrict the follower's recitation.
The Hanafi school relies on the wording transmitted by Abu Sa'id and extends the sunnah to the follower.
5
Apply the ruling
In a congregational prayer, after the imam's takbir, the follower recites the opening supplication silently because it is not part of the qira'ah that the imam carries.
This distinguishes it from the Fatiha, which the follower does not recite behind the imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في تركيب الصلوة

ويستفتح كل مصل (۴۵۷) ثم يتعوّذ سرًا للقراءة فيأتى به المسبوق لا المقتدى ويؤخّر عن تكبيرات العيدين (۴۵۸) ثم يسمّى سرّا ويسمّى في كل ركعة قبل الفاتحة فقط ثم قرأ الفاتحة

تشریح : تحریمہ باندھنے کے بعد سبحانک الخ پڑھے، اور یہ مقتدی بھی پڑھے، کیونکہ یہ قرآت کی طرح نہیں ہے کہ امام کی قرآت مقتدی کی قرآت شمار ہو۔ وجه (۱) یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدري قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قام الى الصلوة بالليل كبر ثم يـقـول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالی جدک ولا اله غیرک. (ترمذی شریف، باب ما يقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ، ص ۱۵۷، نمبر ۲۴۲ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من رأی الاستفتاح بسجا تک ،ص ۱۹ نمبر ۷۷۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجا تک اللھم الخ پڑھنا چاہئے۔
Section on the composition of prayer. And every praying person opens (with istiftah) (457). Then he seeks refuge quietly for recitation; the latecomer (masbuq) says it, not the follower (muqtadi), and it is delayed after the takbirs of the two Eids (458). Then he says the basmala quietly, and he says the basmala in every rak'ah only before the Fatiha. Then he recites the Fatiha. Explanation: After the closing takbir (tahrima), he recites 'Subhanaka Allahumma...', and the follower also recites it, because it is not like recitation (qira'ah) such that the imam's recitation counts for the follower. Proof (1): This is a hadith. From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) stood for prayer at night, he would say the takbir, then say: Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma yaqul 'inda iftitah al-salah, p.157, no.242 / Abu Dawud, Bab man ra'a al-istiftah bi-subhanak, p.19, no.775) From this hadith, it is known that one should recite 'Subhanaka Allahumma...'.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof (marfu' hadith) concerning the opening supplication (du'a al-istiftah) in salah. The author states that every person praying (مصل) recites the opening supplication after the takbirat al-tahrima. This applies to both the imam and the follower (muqtadi), unlike the recitation of the Fatiha which the follower does not recite behind the imam according to the Hanafi school. The proof is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri describing the Prophet's (ﷺ) practice at night: he would say takbir, then recite 'Subhanaka Allahumma...'. This forms the basis for the opening supplication. The text also mentions that the ta'awwudh is done quietly, but that will be covered in the next lesson. The opening supplication is a sunnah for all, including the follower, because it is not considered part of the qira'ah that the imam carries for the follower.

Key Terms
الاستفتاح (al-istiftah): The opening supplication recited after the takbirat al-tahrima, before the ta'awwudh and Fatiha.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has already started; he will complete his missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who recites the opening supplication (istiftah) in congregation?
A) Only the imam
B) Both the imam and the follower (muqtadi)
C) Only the follower (muqtadi)
D) Neither the imam nor the follower

Key Takeaway
The opening supplication is a sunnah recited by everyone in salah after takbir; it is proven by the hadith of Abu Sa'id.

Who Recites Ta'awwudh in Salah?
Ruling on ta'awwudh recitation before Fatiha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who recites ta'awwudh in Hanafi salah, cite the primary dalil, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is linked to qira'ah; the muqtadi does not recite it because he does not recite the Quran.

This lesson examines the ruling on reciting ta'awwudh before the Fatiha in salah. The Hanafi school holds that ta'awwudh is a sunnah for those who actively recite the Quran in prayer, namely the imam, the one praying alone, and the masbuq when completing his rak'ahs. The muqtadi does not recite it. We will explore the Quranic and hadith evidence and see how this ruling differs from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act: reciting ta'awwudh before Fatiha. State the hukm level according to Hanafi fiqh (sunnah) and specify who is obligated to do so.
The act is sunnah, not wajib or fard.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence: Quran 16:98 and the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. Note the type of each dalil (Quran, Sunnah).
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah regarding obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze the imperative 'fasta'idh' in the verse. In Hanafi usul, a command indicates wujub. Explain why the Hanafis interpret it as sunnah (reconciling with the Prophet's practice).
The command is overridden by evidence showing it is sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the Shafi'i position: the muqtadi also recites ta'awwudh. State their proof (the verse is general) and the Hanafi response (muqtadi does not recite).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Conclude that the Hanafi position is the mufta bihi. The practical consequence: the muqtadi omits ta'awwudh, while the imam and masbuq recite it quietly.

Translation: (457) Then he seeks refuge quietly for recitation, and he says 'A'udhu billah'. The latecomer (masbuq) says it, not the follower (muqtadi), and he says it after the extra takbirs of the two Eids. Explanation: Then he says quietly 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'. Those who have to recite (qira'ah) should say ta'awwudh, and those who do not recite should not say ta'awwudh or basmala. Thus the masbuq will recite later, so he will say ta'awwudh and basmalah at that time. After the extra takbirs of the two Eids, he will recite, so he will say ta'awwudh and basmalah after those takbirs. As for the muqtadi, since he will not recite (behind the imam), he will not say ta'awwudh or basmalah. Proof (1): The verse: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan' (Surah al-Nahl 16:98). This verse shows that before reciting the Quran, one should say ta'awwudh. It also shows that ta'awwudh is connected to qira'ah, not to the opening supplication. (2) There is a hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: When the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) stood at night, he would say the takbir... then say: Allahu akbar kabiran three times, a'udhu billahi al-sami' al-alim min al-shaytan al-rajim min hamzihi wa nafkhihi... then he would recite. (Abu Dawud, Bab man ra'a al-istiftah bi-subhanak, p.121, no.775) This hadith shows that recitation comes after ta'awwudh, so ta'awwudh is attached to qira'ah.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding the recitation of ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) before the Fatiha in salah. The author clarifies that the ta'awwudh is recited quietly by those who will recite the Quran in the prayer, namely the imam and the one praying alone, as well as the masbuq (latecomer) when he completes his missed rak'ahs. The muqtadi (follower) does not recite the ta'awwudh because he does not recite the Fatiha behind the imam in Hanafi fiqh. The proof is twofold: first, the Quranic verse (16:98) commanding general seeking refuge before recitation; second, a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing the Prophet (ﷺ) saying ta'awwudh before recitation. The Hanafi school deduces that ta'awwudh is connected to qira'ah, not to the opening supplication, hence its ruling follows that of qira'ah.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): The phrase 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' recited before the Fatiha in salah.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The person following the imam from the beginning of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only the muqtadi

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh is sunnah only for those who actively recite the Quran in salah; the muqtadi omits it because he does not recite.

Basmala Before Fatiha in Salah: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on reciting basmala before Fatiha and only once per prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recitation of basmala in salah, explain the evidence from hadith and athar, and distinguish the practice from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Basmala is recited quietly before the Fatiha in each rak'ah, and once suffices for the entire prayer.

In this passage, the author clarifies the Hanafi position on reciting bismillah during salah. It is a separate sunnah before the Fatiha, not an integral verse, and the follower does not recite it. We also learn that reciting it once at the beginning suffices, and it is not repeated before additional surahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Reciting basmala before the Fatiha in salah. What is the ruling? It is sunnah, recited quietly.
The text says 'آہستہ سے بسم اللہ پڑھے' (recites bismillah quietly).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abu Huraira and an athar from Ibrahim an-Nakha'i. Identify which proof supports each aspect.
Hadith links basmala to Fatiha; athar shows one recitation suffices.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The phrase 'فاقرئوا بسم الله' commands reciting basmala with the Fatiha, indicating it is recited before Fatiha, not separate.
The athar 'اجزاه ذالک' shows that once is sufficient.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position differs from Shafi'i. Shafi'i holds basmala is an integral verse of Fatiha, recited aloud in audible prayers. Hanafi says it is a separate sunnah, recited quietly.
This ikhtilaf affects whether the follower recites it and the manner of recitation.
5
Evaluate the practical thamarah
The practical consequence: in Hanafi prayer, basmala is not recited by the follower, and it is recited only before Fatiha, not before other surahs. In Shafi'i prayer, basmala is recited aloud before Fatiha in audible prayers by everyone.
This difference is significant in congregational settings.

الرحيم ، انها أم القرآن و أم الكتاب و السبع المثاني ، و بسم ا الله الرحمن الرحیم احداها ـ (دارقطنی ، باب وجوب قراءة بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ، ج اول ، ص ۳۰۲ نمبر۱۷۷ ارسنن بیھقی ، باب الدلیل علی ان بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم آسية تامة من الفاتحتہ ، ج خانی جس ۶۷ نمبر ۲۳۹۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو فاتحہ پڑھنے وہی بسم اللہ پڑھے۔ (۱) صرف ایک مرتبہ بسم اللہ پڑھنا کافی ہے، اور سورت سے پہلے نہ پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ابراهيم أنه كان يقول : اذا قرأ الرجل في صلوته مرة واحدة بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ) اجزاه ذالک ) - مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، ۱۹۵ الرجل يقر أبسم الله الرحمن الرحیم ، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۲ نمبر ۴۱۵۸ رمصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب قرآة بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ، ج ثانی ص ۵۸، نمبر ۲۶۰۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بسم اللہ ایک مرتبہ یعنی شروع میں پڑھے۔
Translation (458): Then he says 'Bismillah' quietly, and he says Bismillah in every rak'ah only before the Fatiha. Then he recites the Fatiha. Explanation: After the ta'awwudh, he says 'Bismillah', then recites Surah al-Fatiha. Whoever recites the Fatiha says Bismillah; thus, in the Hanafi school, the follower will not recite the Fatiha, so he will not say Bismillah either. The phrase 'only before the Fatiha' also indicates that he does not say Bismillah before the surah (after the Fatiha). Proof: (1) From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'When you recite Alhamdulillah, then recite Bismillah ar-Rahman ar-Rahim, for it is the Umm al-Quran, Umm al-Kitab, and the seven oft-repeated verses.' (Darqutni, Bab wujub qira'at bismillah, etc.) This hadith shows that whoever recites the Fatiha also recites Bismillah. (1) Reciting Bismillah once in the prayer is sufficient; it is not recited before the surah. For this, there is an athar from Ibrahim an-Nakha'i: 'When a man recites in his prayer 'Bismillah ar-Rahman ar-Rahim' once, that suffices him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, etc.) This athar indicates that Bismillah is recited once, i.e., at the beginning.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof concerning the recitation of the basmala (Bismillah) in salah. The author states that basmala is recited quietly before the Fatiha in every rak'ah. However, only those who recite the Fatiha say it; thus, in Hanafi fiqh, the follower (muqtadi) does not say it. Additionally, basmala is recited only once in the entire prayer (at the beginning of the first rak'ah) and not before the additional surah after the Fatiha. The proof is a hadith from Abu Huraira that links basmala to the Fatiha, and an athar (report) from Ibrahim an-Nakha'i indicating that reciting it once suffices. The Hanafi position is that the basmala is not an independent verse of the Fatiha but is recited for barakah at the start.

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmala): The phrase 'Bismillah ar-Rahman ar-Rahim' recited before the Fatiha in salah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that basmala is a sunnah recited quietly before the Fatiha, once in the entire prayer suffices, and the follower does not recite it.

The Ruling on Saying 'Amin' Quietly After Fatiha
Ruling on saying Amin quietly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that both imam and follower say Amin quietly in Hanafi salah and identify the primary evidence for this ruling.

Core Idea
Amin is said quietly in Hanafi prayer, following the Prophet’s practice.

This lesson addresses the recitation of 'Amin' after the Fatiha in salah. The Hanafi school holds that Amin is a sunnah said quietly by both the imam and the follower, based on clear hadith evidence. Understanding this ruling helps ensure correct prayer practice and distinguishes the Hanafi position from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act under discussion is the utterance of 'Amin' immediately after reciting Surah al-Fatiha in salah.
Amin is a verbal response, not a Quranic recitation.
2
State the ruling
In the Hanafi school, saying Amin is a sunnah (recommended) act, not a fard or wajib. It is said quietly by both the imam and the follower.
This contrasts with the Shafi'i school where the imam says it aloud.
3
Identify the evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith from 'Alqama ibn Wa'il that the Prophet (ﷺ) lowered his voice when saying Amin. The hadith encouraging ta'min (from Abu Huraira) is also cited.
Both hadiths support the practice; the quietness is derived from the explicit lowering of voice.
4
Analyze the mode of recitation
The Hanafi school deduces that Amin should be said quietly because the hadith states the Prophet 'lowered his voice' (khafada biha sawtahu).
The Shafi'i school interprets the 'lowering' as relative, but Hanafis take it literally.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the imam says Amin aloud based on another hadith. The practical difference is audible expression during congregational prayer.
Both positions are documented, but the Hanafi view is relied upon in the school.

Source Text

Translation: (459) And the imam and the follower say 'Amin' quietly. Proof: (1) From Abu Huraira: The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin, for whoever's Amin coincides with the Amin of the angels, his previous sins will be forgiven.' And Ibn Shihab said: The Messenger of Allah would say 'Amin'. (Bukhari, Bab Jahr al-imam bi al-ta'min, p.107, no.780; Muslim, Bab al-tasmi' wa al-tahmid wa al-ta'min, p.76, no.915/410) This hadith shows that both imam and follower say Amin. (2) And the proof for saying Amin quietly is this hadith: From 'Alqama ibn Wa'il from his father that the Prophet (ﷺ) recited 'Ghayr al-maghdubi 'alayhim wa la al-dallin', then said 'Amin' and lowered his voice. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-amin, p.68, no.248; Darqutni, Bab al-ta'min, etc.) This hadith shows that Amin should be said quietly. Translation: (420) Then he recites a surah or three verses. Explanation: After the Fatiha, he joins a surah, or one long verse, or three short verses. Proof: (1) In this hadith: From Abu Sa'id: The Prophet (ﷺ) said: '...and no salah for the one who does not recite al-Hamd (Fatiha) and a surah in an obligatory or other prayer.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi tahrim al-salah wa tahliliha, p.55, no.238; Ibn Majah, Bab al-qira'a khalfa al-imam, p.119, no.839) This indicates that joining a surah after the Fatiha is obligatory like the Fatiha.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage combines two rulings: (1) The recitation of 'Amin' after the Fatiha, and (2) the recitation of a surah (or equivalent) after the Fatiha. The author states that both the imam and the follower say 'Amin' quietly, citing a hadith from Abu Huraira that encourages saying Amin and a hadith from 'Alqama that the Prophet said it quietly. In the Hanafi school, Amin is said quietly by both imam and muqtadi. The second ruling is that after the Fatiha, one must recite a complete surah, or one long verse, or three short verses. This is based on a hadith that says 'no salah for the one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah'. The Hanafi view is that reciting a surah after the Fatiha is wajib (obligatory) in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers and in all rak'ahs of nafl prayers, based on this and other evidence.

Key Terms
التأمين (al-ta'min): The utterance of 'Amin' after reciting the Fatiha in salah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Obligation (Wajib) of Reciting a Surah After Fatiha
Ruling on surah recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that reciting a surah after Fatiha is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard salah and in all rak'ahs of nafl, and identify the primary evidence and the opposing view.

Core Idea
Reciting a surah after Fatiha is wajib; omitting it requires compensation.

This lesson covers the second ruling in the passage: the recitation of a surah (or equivalent) after the Fatiha in salah. The Hanafi school considers this wajib based on a clear hadith, while the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. Understanding this ruling is crucial for correct prayer practice and knowing the consequences of omission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is reciting a complete surah (or three short verses or one long verse) after Surah al-Fatiha in the prayer.
This applies to the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers and all rak'ahs of nafl prayers.
2
State the ruling
According to the Hanafi school, this recitation is wajib (obligatory). It is not fard, but its omission requires sajdah al-sahw if done unintentionally, and the prayer must be repeated if omitted intentionally.
If omitted forgetfully, sajdah al-sahw suffices; if intentionally, the prayer is invalid.
3
Identify the evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'La salata liman lam yaqra' bi al-hamdi wa suratin' (No salah for the one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah).
The negation 'la salata' indicates invalidity, which in Hanafi usul signals obligation (wujub).
4
Analyze the dalala
The phrase 'la salata' is a negation that implies the absence of valid prayer. This is a strong indicator that the mentioned act (reciting surah) is wajib.
The Shafi'i school interprets this as a recommendation due to other evidence.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that reciting a surah after Fatiha is sunnah, not wajib. He bases this on the fact that the Prophet sometimes omitted it and other hadith.
The practical consequence: A Hanafi who omits the surah unintentionally must perform sajdah al-sahw; a Shafi'i's prayer remains valid without it.

Ruku with Takbir and Tranquility
Ruling on ruku with takbir and tranquility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the takbir for ruku and identify the conditions for valid ruku, including tranquility (tuma'nina) and hand placement.

Core Idea
Saying 'Allahu Akbar' while entering ruku is wajib, and tranquility (tuma'nina) is a condition for the validity of ruku.

This passage is a ruling statement (matn) from a Hanafi fiqh text, detailing the actions of ruku. It instructs the worshipper to say takbir while bowing into ruku with tranquility, keeping the head level with the buttocks, and placing the hands on the knees with fingers spread. These details define the proper performance of this pillar of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its components
The passage describes the transition to ruku: saying takbir, entering ruku, maintaining posture (head level, hands on knees).
The text is a matn, so it gives concise rulings.
2
Distinguish the ruling of each component
In Hanafi fiqh, the ruku itself is a pillar (fard), the takbir for ruku is wajib, and tranquility (tuma'nina) is a condition (shart) for validity.
The takbir is not fard; missing it requires sajdah al-sahw.
3
Explain the significance of tranquility
Tuma'nina means a brief pause in the ruku posture. Without it, the ruku is invalid, and the salah must be repeated if the mistake is not corrected.
This is based on the hadith 'la salata liman la yuqimu salbahu'.
4
Note the incomplete description
The passage cuts off mid-sentence; the full matn would likely specify placing hands on knees and possibly the sunnah of spreading fingers.
This lesson covers only the provided portion.

Saying Amin Silently: The Hanafi Position and Its Proof
Ruling on saying Amin silently in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying Amin in prayer and explain the dalil that supports saying it silently.

Core Idea
Both imam and follower say Amin silently — the lower voice follows the Prophet's own practice.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on saying Amin after Surah al-Fatiha in congregational prayer. The source passage presents two hadith: one commanding Amin generally, and another showing the Prophet lowering his voice. Understanding this proof chain will clarify why the Hanafi school holds this act as sunnah muakkadah and why it differs from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying Amin after Surah al-Fatiha. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) for both imam and follower.
The source explicitly states it is sunnah; not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The first hadith (from Abu Hurayra) commands Amin, but does not specify volume. The second hadith (from Alqama) specifies that the Prophet lowered his voice when saying Amin.
Both hadith are ahad (single-chain), thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fa'aminu' in the first hadith indicates a commanded act. In Hanafi usul, a command implies sunnah muakkadah (not obligation), because the hadith is ahad and does not reach the level of wujub. The second hadith provides the modality: 'lowered his voice' indicating silence.
The combination of these two proofs gives the full ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that the imam says Amin loudly, based on a different interpretation of the first hadith and other evidence.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions have textual support.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school prefers the silent position because the second hadith (lowering voice) is specific and not contradicted by the first. The ruling is mufta bihi as sunnah muakkadah.
The later Hanafi masters (e.g., al-Marghinani) affirm this preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۵۹) وامن الامام والماموم سرًا ترجمه : (۴۵۹) اور امام اور مقتدی آہستہ سے آمین کہے۔ وجه: (1) عن ابي هريرة ان النبي عل الله قال : اذا امن الامام فأمنوا فانه من وافق تأمينه تأمين الملائكة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه وقال ابن شهاب وكان رسول الله الله يقول آمين (بخاری شریف، باب جهر الامام بالتا مین ص ۱۰۷ نمبر ۷۸۰ر مسلم شریف ، باب التسميع والتحميد والتأمین ص ۷۶ انمبر ۹۱۵/۴۱۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا امام اور مقتدی دونوں آمین کہے۔(۲) اور آہستہ آمین کہنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علقمة بن وائل عـن ابـيـه ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قرء غير المغضوب عليهم ولا الضالين فقال آمین و خفض بها صوته ترندی ،شریف، باب ماجاء فی الامین ، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۲۴۸ / دار قطنی ، باب التأمين في الصلوة بعد فاتحه الکتاب والجهر بها ، ج اول ص ۳۲۸ نمبر ۶ ۱۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آمین آہستہ کہنا چاہئے ۔
And the imam and the follower say Amin silently.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This is a ruling on saying Amin after Surah al-Fatiha. The text states that both the imam and the follower should say Amin silently. The proof is a hadith from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet said: 'When the imam says Amin, say Amin, for whoever's Amin coincides with the Amin of the angels, his previous sins are forgiven.' Another hadith from Alqama ibn Wa'il reports that the Prophet said Amin after reciting 'ghayril maghdubi alayhim waladhdhallin' and lowered his voice. Therefore, Amin is said silently. In the Hanafi school, this ruling is considered a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah). The imam and follower both say it, but with a low voice to avoid disturbing others.

Key Terms
آمین (Amin): Saying 'Amin' after Surah al-Fatiha in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Remained silent

Key Takeaway
Both imam and follower say Amin silently in prayer; it is sunnah muakkadah.

The Obligation of Reciting a Surah After Fatiha
Ruling with proof for surah recitation after Fatiha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on surah recitation after Fatiha, identify the proof from hadith, and explain why it is classified as wajib rather than fard.

Core Idea
Reciting a surah after Fatiha is wajib in the first two rak'ah of fard and all rak'ah of nafl.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on the additional Quranic recitation after Surah al-Fatiha in salah. The source passage presents a hadith that appears to make this recitation a condition for the prayer's validity. We will explore how the Hanafi school interprets this hadith to derive the obligation (wujub) and clarify the subtle distinction between fard and wajib in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that one must recite either a complete surah, or one long verse equivalent to two or three short verses, or three short verses after Fatiha. Determine the exact legal classification (fard/wajib) from the Hanafi perspective.
The text uses 'fard' loosely; technically it is wajib due to the zanni nature of the dalil.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'لا صلوة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد و سورة' (There is no prayer for the one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah). Identify the source and its reliability.
This hadith is narrated by Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah, classified as ahad (single-chain).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negation of prayer ('لا صلوة') when the surah is omitted indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. Explain how the imperative style and context yield wujub.
The hadith negates the perfection or validity of the prayer without the surah, implying it is an essential component.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Compare with the Shafi'i position, which considers surah recitation after Fatiha as sunnah (recommended), not wajib. Understand the basis of their difference.
Shafi'is interpret the hadith as referring to the Fatiha itself, not the additional surah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the apparent meaning of the hadith and other supporting evidence. Understand why the mufta bihi is wajib and how omission is compensated by sajdah sahwi.
The practical consequence: if a surah is forgotten in the first two rak'ah, sajdah sahwi is required; the prayer remains valid.

The Four Sunnah Acts of Ruku
Ruling on the four sunnah acts of ruku

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunnah acts of ruku and explain the recommended posture according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Four sunnah acts complete ruku: takbir, level back, grip knees with spread fingers, and tasbih thrice.

Ruku is a fundamental pillar of salah, but its perfection lies in observing the sunnah acts. This passage from Thamaratun Najah details the four sunnah acts that the Prophet ﷺ consistently practiced. Understanding these acts will help you perform ruku with the beauty and completeness taught by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunnah acts
Read the passage and list the four acts: (1) saying takbir while going into ruku with itminan, (2) making the head level with the buttocks (i.e., straight back), (3) placing hands on knees with fingers spread, (4) saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' at least three times.
2
Understand the posture requirements
The head should be level with the buttocks, meaning the back is straight, not arched or drooping. Fingers should be spread apart when grasping the knees.
The Hanafi school emphasizes spreading fingers; other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) keep them together.
3
Learn the minimum tasbih
The minimum is three repetitions of 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem'. More is recommended.
This is the least that fulfills the sunnah; additional repetitions are meritorious.
4
Recognize the legal status
All four acts are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah). They are not fard or wajib, but leaving them repeatedly is blameworthy.
The proofs are from the continuous practice of the Prophet ﷺ.

Then he says takbir while going into ruku with tranquility, making his head level with his buttocks, taking hold of his knees with his hands with fingers spread apart, and glorifies [his Lord] three times; this is the minimum.

Commentary
This passage describes the manner of going into ruku. The author lists four sunnah acts: (1) He says 'Allahu Akbar' as he goes into ruku with tranquility (i'tidal), not rushing. (2) He makes his head and back level so that his head is even with his buttocks, meaning the spine is straight and the back is flat. (3) He places his hands on his knees with fingers spread, grasping firmly. (4) He says 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' three times, which is the minimum. The proofs for these acts are from the Prophet's practice as transmitted in previous hadith (the author says they have passed). These are considered sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ركوع (ruku): Bowing in prayer.
اطمئنان (itminan): Tranquility, motionlessness in a posture.
سبحان ربي العظيم (Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem): Glory be to my Lord, the Magnificent.

Standing Up from Ruku: Tadil al-Arkan, Tasmi', and Tahmid
Ruling on tadil al-arkan and tasmi/tahmid in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings of tadil al-arkan (wajib) and the tasmi' and tahmid (sunnah) for imam, munfarid, and follower, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Tadil al-arkan is wajib; tasmi' and tahmid are sunnah — follower omits the tasmi'.

In the standing after ruku (qawmah), the Hanafi school distinguishes between the obligation of tranquility (tadil al-arkan) and the sunnah utterances of tasmi' and tahmid. This passage from Thamaratun Najah clearly outlines who says what based on the Prophet's practice, and clarifies that the follower does not say 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its rulings
What act is being ruled upon? The standing after ruku (qawmah). Identify the three rulings: tadil al-arkan is wajib; tasmi' and tahmid are sunnah; and the difference between imam/munfarid and follower.
The passage breaks it into three numbered points.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: from Abu Hurayra (Bukhari, Tirmidhi) and Abu Awfa (Muslim). Identify that both are ahad (non-mutawatir).
The hadith show the Prophet's consistent practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet said both tasmi' and tahmid when leading prayer; there is no report of him saying only one. This establishes the sunnah for imam and munfarid. For the follower, the hadith does not show them saying tasmi', so they suffice with tahmid.
Evidence from absence of reports.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that tasmi' and tahmid are sunnah for all, including the follower, based on a general command to follow the imam.
A legitimate difference of ijtihad.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon because the hadith evidence specifically shows the imam saying tasmi' and the follower being silent. The mufta bihi is that the follower says only tahmid.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۶۲) پھر سر اٹھائے اور اطمینان سے کہے سمع اللہ لمن حمدہ، امام اور منفر دہوتو ہر بنا لک الحمد بھی کہے، اور مقتدی صرف ربنا لک الحمد، پراکتفاء کرے۔ تشریح : یہاں تین باتیں ہیں [1] ایک بات یہ ہے کہ رکوع سے کھڑا ہو تو اطمینان سے کھڑا ہو جسکو تعدیل ارکان کہتے ہیں، کیونکہ یہ واجب ہے۔ [۲] دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ سمع اللہ لمن حمدہ ، امام اور جو تنہا پڑھ رہا ہو دونوں کہیں گے، مقتدی سمع اللہ لمن حمدہ، نہیں کہے گا ، وہ صرف ربنا لک الحمد، کہے گا [۳] اور تیسری بات یہ ہے کہ، امام اور منفرد ربنا لک الحمد بھی کہیں گےا۔ وجه : (1) عن ابي هريرة قال كان النبى الله الله اذا قال سمع الله لمن حمدہ قال اللهم لک الحمد ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب ما يقول الامام ومن خلفه اذا رفع رأسه من الركوع ،ص ۱۲۹، نمبر ۷۹۵ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ما يقول الرجل اذا رفع راسہ من الرکوع ص ۷۳، نمبر ۲۶۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام سمیع اور تحمید دونوں کہے گا (۲)۔ عن ابی اوفی قال : كان رسول الله لا اذا رفع ظهره من الركوع قال : سمع الله لمن حمده ، اللهم ربنا ! لک الحمد ، ملء السماوات وملء الارض ، و ملء ما شئت من شيء بعد - (مسلم شریف، باب ما یقول اذا رفع رأسه من الركوع، ص ۱۹۸، نمبر ۴۷۶ / ۱۰۶۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور دونوں کہا کرتے تھے۔ اسلئے امام دونوں کہے۔
Then he raises his head and stands with tranquility, saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'; if he is imam or munfarid, he also says 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. The follower suffices with 'Rabbana lakal hamd'.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage addresses the standing after ruku (qawmah). The author explains three points: (1) One must stand upright with tranquility after raising from ruku; this is called tadil al-arkan and is wajib. (2) The imam and the one praying alone say both 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' (Allah hears the one who praises Him) and 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (Our Lord, to You is praise). (3) The follower only says the tahmid (Rabbana lakal hamd) and does not say the tasmi' (Sami'a Allah...). This is based on hadith from Abu Hurayra and Abu Awfa showing the Prophet's practice. In the Hanafi school, tadil al-arkan in qawmah is wajib, and the tasmi' and tahmid are sunnah.

Key Terms
تعدیل ارکان (tadil al-arkan): Standing straight after ruku with tranquility.
سمع اللہ لمن حمدہ (Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah): Allah hears the one who praises Him.
ربنا لک الحمد (Rabbana lakal hamd): Our Lord, to You is praise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only munfarid

Key Takeaway
Tadil al-arkan is wajib; the tasmi' is for imam and munfarid only, and the follower says only the tahmid.

Takbir when Going to Sujud
Ruling on takbir when going to sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on saying takbir when moving to sujud and identify the sunnah nature of this action.

Core Idea
Saying takbir when going to sujud is a sunnah muakkadah, not a wajib.

This lesson addresses a specific moment in the prayer: the descent to sujud. The text clearly instructs to say takbir while moving down. Although the proof is not repeated here, it rests on the consistent practice of the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding this sunnah helps perfect the prayer's form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act described? During which movement is takbir said? The text says: 'Then he says takbir while going down for sujud.' The ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
The act is saying 'Allahu Akbar' while descending into prostration.
2
Analyze the evidence
Although the proof is not presented here, the ruling is based on the Prophet's ﷺ practice and the consensus of the Companions. In Hanafi usul, such a consistent practice elevates the act to sunnah muakkadah.
In earlier sections (not in this chunk), the dalil from hadith is cited.
3
Differentiate from wajib
Sunnah muakkadah means recommended but not obligatory. Omitting it does not invalidate the prayer, nor require sujud as-sahw. This contrasts with wajib actions like takbirat al-ihram.
Wajib omissions require compensation; sunnah omissions do not.

The Sunnah Manner of Sujud: Sequence and Posture
Ruling on the sunnah acts in sujud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunnah acts of sujud in their correct sequence and explain the requirement of tranquility.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sujud: knees first, then hands, then face between palms, with stillness.

The manner of sujud is a crucial part of salah. While the basic obligation is to prostrate, the Prophet (peace be upon him) taught a specific sequence and posture that enhance the prayer. In this lesson, we examine the four sunnah acts of sujud as described in the Hanafi text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunnah acts
From the text, list the four actions described: placing knees, placing hands, placing the face between the palms, and ensuring tranquility on the nose and forehead.
2
Understand the sequence
Note the order: knees first, then hands, then face between the palms. This is the recommended Hanafi sequence.
Reversing the order is considered missing a sunnah.
3
Recognize the face position
The face should be placed between the palms, with the nose and forehead touching the ground.
Some schools place the face outside the hands.
4
Appreciate tranquility (itminan)
The word 'اطمئنان' indicates a requirement of stillness in sujud, not just a momentary touch.
Tranquility is necessary for the sunnah to be complete.
5
Note cross-madhhab variation
The Hanafi position is that the sequence is sunnah; other schools may have different orders or consider some acts obligatory.
Differences are legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۶۴) پھر دونوں گھٹنے رکھے ، پھر دونوں ہاتھ رکھے، پھر دونوں ہتھیلیوں کے درمیان چہرہ رکھے ، اور ناک اور پیشانی پر اطمینان سے سجدہ کرے۔ تشریح یہاں سجدے کی چار سنتیں ہیں [1] زمین پر پہلے دونوں گھٹنے رکھے ۔ [۲] پھر دونوں ہاتھ رکھے۔[۳] پھر دونوں ہتھیلیاں [کے درمیان چہرہ رکھے] [۴] اور ناک اور پیشانی پر اطمینان سے سجدہ کرے۔
Then he places his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms, and prostrates with tranquility on his nose and forehead.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage describes the sunnah manner of sujud. Four sunnah acts: (1) Place the knees on the ground first. (2) Then place the hands on the ground. (3) Then place the face between the palms, so that the forehead and nose are on the ground. (4) Ensure tranquility (itminan) in sujud. The order (knees, then hands, then face) is the recommended sequence. The author notes these are sunnah, and the proofs have been given earlier.

Key Terms
سجود (sujud): Prostration in prayer.
اطمئنان (itminan): Tranquility, stillness in a posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Knees, hands, face
C) Face, hands, knees
D) All at once

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah for sujud is to place knees, then hands, then face between palms, and remain still.

Rulings on Post-Ruku' Standing, Duas, and Prostration
Rulings on post-ruku' standing, tashmi', tahmid, and sujud method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for the actions after ruku' (qawmah, tashmi', tahmid) and the method of sujud, and identify which actions are wajib versus sunnah.

Core Idea
In Hanafi prayer, tranquility after ruku' is wajib; imam says both tashmi' and tahmid, but follower says only tahmid.

After rising from ruku', there are specific recommended and obligatory actions. The Hanafi school distinguishes between what the imam, the follower, and the one praying alone recite. This passage from a classical text lays out these rulings with their proofs from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
List each action described: qawmah (standing), tashmi' and tahmid, takbir for sujud, order of limbs in sujud, tasbih, and separation of limbs. Determine the hukm level for each (wajib or sunnah).
The text explicitly states that ta'dil al-arkan (standing calmly) is wajib; all others are sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
For each ruling, identify the hadith cited. The passage quotes from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi.
The follower-only-tahmid ruling is derived from hadith where the Prophet said both when acting as imam, but the passage does not give a separate hadith for the follower's omission; it is based on usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. For example, the hadith of Abu Hurairah shows the Prophet combined tashmi' and tahmid, so the imam should do likewise.
The follower's omission is inferred from the fact that the follower is not leading and thus responds with praise alone.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text mentions no internal Hanafi dispute, but there is cross-madhhab difference: Shafi'i school holds that the follower also says tashmi'.
The Hanafi position is that the follower says only tahmid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is as stated: follower says only 'Rabbana laka al-hamd'; sujud with knees first; tasbih at least three times; separation of limbs for men.
These rulings are from zahir al-riwayah and are considered mufta bihi.

نہیں کہے گا ، وہ صرف ربنا لک الحمد، کہے گا [۳] اور تیسری بات یہ ہے کہ، امام اور منفرد ربنا لک الحمد بھی کہیں گےا۔ وجه : (1) عن ابي هريرة قال كان النبى الله الله اذا قال سمع الله لمن حمدہ قال اللهم لک الحمد ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب ما يقول الامام ومن خلفه اذا رفع رأسه من الركوع ،ص ۱۲۹، نمبر ۷۹۵ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ما يقول الرجل اذا رفع راسہ من الرکوع ص ۷۳، نمبر ۲۶۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام سمیع اور تحمید دونوں کہے گا (۲)۔ عن ابی اوفی قال

ترجمه : (۴۶۳) پھر سجدے کے لئے جھکتے ہوئے تکبیر کہے۔ تشریح : قومہ کے بعد سجدہ میں جاتے ہوئے اللہ اکبر کہے۔ دلیل گزر چکی ہے۔۔ خارا: خر سے مشتق ہے، جھکتے ہوئے۔ ترجمه : (۴۶۴) پھر دونوں گھٹنے رکھے ، پھر دونوں ہاتھ رکھے، پھر دونوں ہتھیلیوں کے درمیان چہرہ رکھے ، اور ناک اور پیشانی پر اطمینان سے سجدہ کرے۔ تشریح یہاں سجدے کی چار سنتیں ہیں [1] زمین پر پہلے دونوں گھٹنے رکھے ۔ [۲] پھر دونوں ہاتھ رکھے۔[۳] پھر دونوں ہتھیلیاں رکھے [۴] اور چوتھی سنت ہے کہ صرف ناک پر یا پیشانی پر سجدہ نہ کرے بلکہ دونوں پر سجدہ کرے، ان میں سے اصل پیشانی ہے
وجه : (۱) عن وائل بن حجر قال رأيت رسول الله الله اذا سجد يضع ركبتيه قبل يديه و اذا نهض رفع يــديــه قبل ركبتيه - ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء في وضع الركبتين قبل اليدين في السجو د ص ۷۴ نمبر ۲۶۸ ابوداود شریف، باب کیف يضع ركبتيه قبل يديه، ص ۱۳۰، نمبر ۸۳۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سجدہ میں جاتے وقت پہلے گھٹنے رکھے بعد میں ہاتھ رکھے ، اور اٹھتے وقت پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے بعد میں گھٹا اٹھائے۔ (۲) سجدہ دونوں ہتھیلیوں کے درمیان کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قلت للبراء بن عازب اين كان النبي الله يضع وجهه اذا سجد؟ فقال بين كفيه ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء این یضع الرجل وجه اذ اسجد، ج ۷۵، نمبر ۲۷۱ مسلم شریف ، باب وضع یدہ الیمنی علی الیسری بعد تکبیرة الاحرام ، الخ ص۱۷۰ نمبر ۸۹۶/۴۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سجدے کے وقت چہرے کو دونوں ہتھیلیوں کے درمیان رکھے۔
ترجمه : (۴۶۵) تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی الاعلی“ کہے، اور یہ ادنی درجہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن مسعود قال : قال رسول الله الله اذا ركع احدكم فليقل ثلاث مرات : سبحان ربی العظيم وذلک ادناه، فاذا سجد فليقل سبحان ربی الاعلى ثلاثا ، و ذالک ادناه . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب مقدار الرکوع والسجود ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۸۸۶ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی التسبيح في الركوع والسجود، ص ۶۰ نمبر (۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی الاعلی ، کہے یادنی مرتبہ ہے۔ ترجمه : (۴۶۶) اور الگ رکھے اپنے پیٹ کو زانو سے اور بازوکو بغلوں سے اگر از دحام نہ ہو ، اور ہاتھ اور پاؤں کی انگلیوں کو قبلہ رخ رکھے۔
تشریح : مرد سجدے میں اپنے پیٹ کو زانوں سے الگ رکھے ، اور بازوکو بغل سے الگ رکھے بشرطیکہ بھیٹر نہ ہو لیکن اگر بھیڑ ہو تو تھوڑا ساسکڑ سکتا ہے، اور ہاتھ اور پاؤں کی انگلیوں کو قبلہ رخ رکھے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بغل کو ران سے الگ رکھو۔ عن مالك بن بحينة ان رسول الله الا الله كان اذا صلی فرج بين يديه حتى يبدو بیاض ابطيه. (بخاری شریف، باب پہدی ضعیه و یجافی جنبه في السجود ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۸۰۷ مسلم شریف ، باب الاعتدال في السجود ووضع الکفین علی الارض ، ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۱۱۰۵/۴۹۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغل کو ران سے اور پیٹ سے اتنا الگ رکھے کہ آدمی پیچھے سے اس کی بغل کی سفیدی دیکھ سکے ۔ (۲) یـسـتـقبــل بـاطراف رجليه القبلة قال ابو حمید عن النبی الله . (بخاری شریف، باب يستقبل باطراف رجلیہ القبلۃ، ص۱۳۱، نمبر ۸۰۸) (۳)فقال ابو حمید الساعدي انا كنت احفظكم لصلوة رسول الله ..... فاذا سجد وضع يديه غير مفترش ولا قابضهما الله
A section on the composition of prayer. Making his head level with his back, taking his knees with his hands, separating his fingers, and he glorifies three times, and that is the minimum. (462) Then he raises his head and stands calmly saying 'Allah hears the one who praises Him, our Lord to You be praise' if he is an imam or alone. And the follower suffices with the tahmid. (463) Then he says the takbir while bending for prostration. (464) Then he places his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms, and prostrates with his nose and forehead calmly. (465) Glorifying three times, and that is the minimum. (466) And he separates his belly from his thighs and his arms from his sides.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the actions following ruku' and the method of sujud. The text first reviews the sunan of ruku' (ruku' sunan: takbir with tranquility, level head, grasping knees with spread fingers, and at least three tasbihs). Then it moves to the qawmah (standing after ruku'). It clarifies that the imam and the one praying alone should say both 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' (tashmi') and 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (tahmid). The follower (muqtadi) says only the tahmid. This is proven by hadith from Abu Hurairah and Abu Awfa. The rising must be with tranquility (ta'dil al-arkan), which is wajib. Next, the takbir while going into sujud is sunnah. The sujud itself has specific sunan: place knees first, then hands, then face between the palms, prostrating on the nose and forehead with tranquility. The hadith from Wa'il ibn Hujr and Bara' ibn 'Azib support this order. Then at least three tasbihs of 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' are sunnah. Finally, a man should separate his belly from his thighs and his arms from his sides, and face the fingertips of his hands and feet towards the qiblah, provided there is no crowding. This is supported by hadith from Malik ibn Bujainah and Abu Humaid. All these rulings are based on authentic ahadith, and the Hanafi school follows them as sunnah mu'akkadah or wajib as specified.

Key Terms
تعديل الأركان (ta'dil al-arkan): Performing each posture of prayer with tranquility and calmness, not rushing.
سمع الله لمن حمده (sami'a Allahu liman hamidah): Statement said by the one praying to invoke Allah's response to praise, a sunnah upon rising from ruku'.
ربنا لك الحمد (rabbana laka al-hamd): Praise to Allah, said after tashmi' or by follower as the only response.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does the follower (muqtadi) say when the imam rises from ruku'?
A) Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah
B) Rabbana laka al-hamd
C) Both A and B
D) Subhana Rabbiyal A'la

Key Takeaway
The follower in Hanafi prayer says only 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' after ruku', not 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', and tranquility (ta'dil al-arkan) is wajib.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Rulings of Sujud: Nose, Forehead, and Tasbih
Ruling with proof on the required elements of sujud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum elements of sujud: placing both nose and forehead firmly, and reciting 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' three times, and explain the evidence for the tasbih being wajib.

Core Idea
In sujud, both nose and forehead must touch the ground, and the tasbih three times is wajib—this is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text presents two key requirements of prostration: the parts of the face that must be placed on the ground and the minimum glorification. While the placement is a sunnah muakkadah, the tasbih is considered wajib by the relied-upon view. Let us examine the evidence and the reasoning behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage first states that one must prostrate with both nose and forehead firmly placed (mutma'innan) and that it is not sufficient to use only one. It then states that one should say 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' three times, and that is the minimum.
These are two separate obligations: a physical condition and a verbal obligation.
2
Locate the dalil for the tasbih
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud in which the Prophet commands to say the tasbih three times in ruku and sujud. Note the imperative 'falyuqul' (let him say) and the phrase 'dhalika adnahu' (that is its minimum).
The imperative indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
According to the Hanafi principle, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the imperative indicates obligation). There is no qarīnah (contextual evidence) to divert it from obligation. The word 'adnahu' confirms that three is the least required.
This is why the mufta bihi is that the tasbih is wajib.
4
Analyze the placement ruling
The passage states that the fourth sunnah is to prostrate on both nose and forehead, not only one. The forehead is considered the original part. This is a sunnah muakkadah, so deliberately abandoning it is disliked.
The hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr about knees and hands is about the manner of going into sujud, not the parts required.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The tasbih being wajib vs sunnah affects whether sajdah al-sahw is required if one omits it. In the Hanafi school, if a wajib is left, sajdah al-sahw becomes necessary.
This is a practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text

الله

ترجمه : (۴۶۵) تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی الاعلی“ کہے، اور یہ ادنی درجہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن مسعود قال : قال رسول الله الله اذا ركع احدكم فليقل ثلاث مرات : سبحان ربی العظيم وذلک ادناه، فاذا سجد فليقل سبحان ربی الاعلى ثلاثا ، و ذالک ادناه . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب مقدار الرکوع والسجود ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۸۸۶ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی التسبيح في الركوع والسجود، ص ۶۰ نمبر (۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی الاعلی ، کہے یادنی مرتبہ ہے۔
Section on the composition of prayer. With his nose and forehead firmly placed (465) glorifying three times, and that is the minimum (466) and he keeps his stomach away from his thighs and his arms from his sides... Place [4] and the fourth sunnah is that he should not prostrate only on the nose or only on the forehead, but rather prostrate on both, among which the forehead is the original. Evidence: (1) From Wa'il ibn Hujr: I saw the Messenger of Allah when he prostrated, he placed his knees before his hands, and when he rose, he raised his hands before his knees. (2) Prostrate between the two palms: I asked al-Bara' ibn 'Azib: Where would the Prophet place his face when he prostrated? He said: Between his palms. Translation of (465): He says ‘Subhana Rabbiyal A'la’ three times, and that is the minimum. Evidence: (1) From Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah said: When one of you bows, let him say three times: Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azim, and that is the minimum; and when he prostrates, let him say three times: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la, and that is the minimum.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm wa dalil) on the obligatory elements of prostration (sajdah). The author, first citing the matn, states that during sujud one must place both nose and forehead firmly on the ground (mutma'innan). He then clarifies that it is not sufficient to place only the nose or only the forehead; both are required, though the forehead is the primary part. He then moves to the tasbih: the minimum is to say 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' three times, as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud. Additionally, he provides evidence for the manner of going into sujud: the knees should be placed before the hands when going down, and hands raised before knees when getting up (hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr). Also, the face should be placed between the palms (hadith of al-Bara'). These are recommended practices (sunnah) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تسبیح (tasbih): The act of glorifying Allah, specifically saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' in sujud.
ادنی (adna): Minimum; the least amount that fulfills the requirement.
مطمئنا (mutma'innan): Being at ease, still, and settled in a posture; in sujud, it means pressing the nose and forehead firmly onto the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of times one should say 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' in prostration according to the hadith cited?
A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Seven times

Key Takeaway
The minimum tasbih in sujud is three times, and in the Hanafi school it is wajib; additionally, sujud must be on both the nose and forehead, with the forehead being primary.

The Sunnah of Tajafi for Men in Sujud
Commands men to keep stomach away from thighs and arms from sides

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah posture for men during sujud and explain the exception for crowding.

Core Idea
Men must keep stomach and arms away in sujud unless crowded; it's a sunnah muakkadah.

In this lesson, we examine the recommended posture for men during prostration. The Hanafi school emphasizes tajafi—keeping the stomach away from the thighs and the arms away from the sides—based on the explicit practice of the Prophet. However, the scholars also recognized practical constraints, allowing slight contraction when the mosque is crowded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage to determine what posture is recommended for men in sujud. The text says to keep the stomach away from the knees and arms away from the sides.
This is a sunnah (recommended) act, not obligatory.
2
Find the exception
Note the condition 'if no crowding' and the allowance to contract slightly when there is crowding. This shows flexibility in applying the sunnah.
The exception prevents undue hardship in crowded congregations.
3
Examine the evidence
The passage cites the hadith of Malik ibn Buhayna: the Prophet separated his arms until the whiteness of his armpits could be seen. Identify the source (Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim).
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning, giving strong proof.
4
Understand the proof
In Hanafi usul, the fi'l (action) of the Prophet indicates sunnah unless there is evidence of obligation. The extreme separation emphasizes high recommendation.
The whiteness indicates clear visibility, not just slight separation.
5
Apply the ruling
State the operative ruling: it is sunnah muakkadah for men to perform tajafi unless crowding prevents it. If omitted, the prayer is valid but deficient.
This is the mufta bihi position.

(بخاری شریف، باب پہدی ضعیه و یجافی جنبه في السجود ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۸۰۷ مسلم شریف ، باب الاعتدال في السجود ووضع الکفین علی الارض ، ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۱۱۰۵/۴۹۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغل کو ران سے اور پیٹ سے اتنا الگ رکھے کہ آدمی پیچھے سے اس کی بغل کی سفیدی دیکھ سکے ۔ (۲) یـسـتـقبــل بـاطراف رجليه القبلة قال ابو حمید عن النبی الله . (بخاری شریف، باب يستقبل باطراف رجلیہ القبلۃ، ص۱۳۱، نمبر ۸۰۸) (۳)فقال ابو حمید الساعدي انا كنت احفظكم لصلوة رسول الله ..... فاذا سجد وضع يديه غير مفترش ولا قابضهما الله
Translation of (466): And he should keep his stomach away from his knees and his arms from his sides, if there is no crowding, and direct the fingers of his hands and feet towards the qiblah. Explanation: A man in prostration should keep his stomach away from his knees, and his arms away from his sides, provided there is no crowding; but if there is crowding, he may contract slightly. And he should direct the fingers of his hands and feet towards the qiblah. Evidence: (1) In this hadith: Keep the armpit away from the thigh. From Malik ibn Buhayna: The Messenger of Allah used to separate his arms when praying such that the whiteness of his armpits could be seen. (2) He directs the tips of his feet towards the qiblah. Abu Humayd said from the Prophet. (3) Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi said: I am the most knowledgeable of you in the prayer of the Messenger of Allah... when he prostrated, he placed his hands not spread out nor clenched.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for men's posture during sujud. The author explains that a man should keep his stomach away from his thighs and his arms away from his sides, unless there is crowding (e.g., in a jammed mosque), in which case slight contraction is allowed. This is to ensure proper humility and to follow the Prophet's practice. The main evidence is the hadith of Malik ibn Buhayna that the Prophet separated his arms so much that the whiteness of his armpits could be seen. Additionally, fingers of both hands and feet should be directed towards the qiblah, as recorded by Abu Humayd. These actions are sunnah (recommended) for men.

Key Terms
تجافی (tajafi): To keep away; specifically, separating the stomach from the thighs and arms from the sides during sujud.
ضم (damm): To contract or bring together; here, the opposite of tajafi, done by women.
قبلہ رخ (qiblah rukh): Facing the qiblah; directing the fingers of hands and feet towards the qiblah during sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a man do with his arms and stomach during sujud?
A) Keep them close to the body
B) Keep them away from the sides and thighs
C) Place his arms on the ground spread out
D) Contract them slightly

Key Takeaway
Tajafi is a sunnah muakkadah for men unless crowding prevents it; following it perfects the prayer but omission does not invalidate.

Directing Fingers of Hands and Feet to the Qiblah in Sujud
Direct fingers of hands and feet towards qiblah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah of directing fingers to the qiblah during sujud and cite the evidence from the hadith of Abu Humayd.

Core Idea
Both hands and feet fingers should face the qiblah in sujud; it's a sunnah for men and women.

This lesson focuses on another sunnah posture in sujud: directing the fingers of both hands and feet towards the qiblah. The Hanafi school considers this a recommended practice based on the recorded practice of the Prophet. Unlike tajafi, this applies to both men and women, enhancing the orientation of the whole body towards the House of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah
Read the passage to determine which body parts should be directed towards the qiblah. The text says to direct the fingers of the hands and feet.
This includes both sets of fingers.
2
Recognize the scope
Note that this sunnah applies to all worshippers, regardless of gender. It is not exclusive to men.
The author does not specify a gender exception, unlike for tajafi.
3
Find the evidence
The passage references the hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi: 'He directs the tips of his feet towards the qiblah.' The full hadith also mentions hand placement.
The hadith is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari.
4
Analyze the proof
The fi'l of the Prophet in this context is taken as evidence of sunnah. The instruction to direct fingers implies conscious alignment.
The lack of a command (amr) indicates sunnah, not wujub.
5
Apply the ruling
State the operative ruling: it is sunnah muakkadah to turn the fingers of both hands and feet towards the qiblah during sujud. Omission does not invalidate the prayer.
This is a point emphasized in Hanafi fiqh.

Women's Posture in Sujud: Lowering and Compactness
Prescribes women to lower themselves and stick belly to thighs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended posture for a woman in sujud according to the Hanafi school and identify the proofs that establish it as sunnah.

Core Idea
Women should prostrate compactly, sticking belly to thighs, for modesty; men should be spread out.

This lesson focuses on a specific ruling within the salah: the posture of a woman during prostration. While men are commanded to adopt a spacious posture (tajafi), women are instructed to lower themselves and remain compact, with belly pressed against thighs. This distinction is rooted in the principle of modesty (satr) and is supported by multiple prophetic traditions and companion practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the passage and extract the specific posture prescribed for women in sujud.
Key terms: takhfid (lowering) and ilzaq (sticking belly to thighs).
2
Understand the rationale
Identify the reason given for this posture. The passage mentions 'satr' (modesty).
Modesty is a central principle in women's prayer rulings.
3
Analyze the primary proof
Examine the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'He commanded men to do tajafi and women to do infikhad.'
The command (amr) indicates sunnah in Hanafi usul due to being ahad.
4
Determine the legal level (hukm)
Conclude whether this posture is fard, wajib, sunnah, etc. The text and analysis show it is sunnah muakkadah.
Not obligatory because the evidence is ahad and the rationale of modesty is a recommendation.

And the woman lowers and sticks her belly to her thighs (468) and sits between the two prostrations placing his hands on his thighs being at ease (469) then he says Allahu Akbar and prostrates. And he directs the tips of his feet towards the qiblah. (Bukhari... the hadith about sitting in tashahhud). From this hadith it is known that during prostration the toes should be pointed towards the qiblah. And it also indicates that the fingers of the hands should also be towards the qiblah. (4) In this hadith from Aisha: The Prophet when he prostrated placed his hands facing the qiblah. Vocabulary: jani: keep away; fakhidh: thigh; 'adud: upper arm; ibt: armpit; zumah: crowding. Translation of (467): And the woman lowers and sticks her belly to her knees. Explanation: The woman should prostrate lowering herself, and stick her belly to her knees, because it is better for her modesty. Evidence: (1) Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: The best rows for men are the first, and for women the last, and he commanded men to keep away (tajafi) in their prostrations, and women to lower themselves. (2) Abdullah ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah said: When a woman sits in prayer, she should place one thigh on the other, and when she prostrates, she should stick her belly to her thighs, as that is more concealing for her. (3) The saying of a Companion: Ali said: When a woman prostrates, let her contract and bring her thighs together. (4) Ibn Abbas: When asked about the prayer of a woman, he said: She should gather and contract. From these hadiths and effects it is known that a woman should remain contracted in prostration and stick her belly to her thighs in order to achieve maximum modesty; this is better for her.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm wa dalil) on the woman's posture in sujud. The author instructs that a woman should lower herself (takhfid) and stick her belly to her thighs, i.e., make herself compact, in contrast to men. The reason given is modesty (satr): this posture is more concealing. The proofs include several hadiths and sayings of companions: (1) The Prophet commanded men to keep away and women to lower. (2) The Prophet explicitly instructed women to stick belly to thighs for maximum concealment. (3) Ali and Ibn Abbas also recommended contraction. These actions are sunnah (recommended) for women.

Key Terms
تخفض (takhfid): To lower; specifically for women, to lower the body in sujud, i.e., not to elevate the posterior but rather keep close to the ground.
تلزق (talzaq): To stick; the woman should stick her belly to her thighs in sujud for modesty.
ستر (satr): Modesty; covering; the reason for the woman's compact posture is to better conceal her body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Rulings on Prostration Posture and Movements
Explaining sunnah postures in prostration, sitting, and rising with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah postures for prostration, sitting, and rising in prayer, and distinguish the women's prostration posture with its evidence.

Core Idea
Men prostrate with limbs apart; women prostrate compactly – both are sunnah established by specific hadith.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text details the recommended postures during prostration and transitions in prayer, citing hadith evidence. Understanding these rulings ensures your prayer follows the Prophetic model as understood by the Hanafi school, especially the distinction between men's and women's postures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
Determine what action is being ruled upon (e.g., prostration posture for men, women, sitting, rising) and classify its hukm (here sunnah mu'akkadah).
For women, the ruling is mustahabb due to modesty, but still sunnah-like.
2
Locate the specific dalil for each posture
Find the hadith or athar cited by the author for each posture (e.g., Bukhari for sitting, Ibn Abi Shaybah for hand placement, Bayhaqi for women).
The author quotes multiple chains to strengthen the evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
Explain how the wording or action in the hadith directly indicates the prescribed posture. For example, the command 'lower' for women shows the compact prostration.
Key: the Prophet's action or command is the proof.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on women's prostration
Identify that some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may treat women's prostration like men's, while Hanafis distinguish based on modesty hadith.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is supported by specific evidence.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Conclude that the Hanafi view is mufta bihi due to the strength and specificity of its hadith evidence.
The author relies on these proofs; the ruling is applied in practice.
