فصل في تركيب الصلوة
ابطيه في غير زحمة موجها اصابع يديه ورجليه نحو القبلة(٤٦٧) والمرأة تخفض وتلزق بطنها بفخذيها (٤٦٨) وجلس بين السجدتين واضعا يديه على فخذيه مطمئنا (٤٦٩) ثم كبر وسجد واستقبل باطراف اصابع رجليه القبلة .
(بخاری شریف، باب یہ الجلوس في التشهد ص١٣٤، نمبر ٨٢٨ سنن المحقی ، باب ينصب قدميه ويستقبل باطراف اصابعهما القبلة ، ج ثانی، ص ١٦٧ نمبر ٢٧١٧) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ کی حالت میں پاؤں کی انگلیاں قبلہ کی طرف رکھنا چاہئے۔ اور اس کا بھی اشارہ ہے کہ ہاتھ کی انگلیاں بھی قبلہ ہی کی جانب ہوں ۔ (٤) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا سجد وضع يديه وجاه القبلة . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من كان يقول اذ اسجد فلیوجہ ید یہ الی القبلة ، ج ثانی، ص ٢٣٦، نمبر ٢٧١٢) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور قبلہ کی طرف ہاتھ کیا کرتے تھے۔
لغت : جانی: دور رکھے۔ فخذ : ران عضد : بازو۔ابط: بغل زحمۃ : بھیڑ۔
ترجمه : (٤٦٧) اور عورت پست ہو کر پیٹ کو گھٹنوں سے ملا دے۔
تشریح : عورت پست ہو کر سجدہ کرے گی ، اور پیٹ کو گھٹنوں سے ملا دے گی۔ کیونکہ ستر کے اعتبار سے یہی اس کے لئے بہتر ہے۔
وجه : (١) عن ابي سعيد الخدری صاحب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن رسول الله انه قال خير صفوف الرجال الاول و خير صفوف النساء الصف الاخرو كان يأمر الرجال ان يتجافوا في سجودهم و يأمر النساء ينخفضن في سجودهن - ( سنن بیھقی ، باب ما یستحب للمرأة من ترك التجافي في الركوع والسجود ، ج ثانی ،ص٣١٤، نمبر ٣١٩٨)۔ (٢) عن عبد الله ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا جلست المرأة في الصلوة وضعت فخذها على فخذها الاخرى واذا سجدت الصقت بطنها في فخذها كأستر ما يكون لها - ( سنن بیھقی ، باب ما يستحب للمرأة من ترك التجافى فى الركوع والسجود، ج ثانی، ص ١٣١٤، نمبر ٣١٩٩) (٣) قول صحابی میں ہے۔ عن علي قال : اذا سجدت المرأة فلتحتفر و لتضم فخذيها (٤) عن ابن عباس أنه سئل عن صلوة المرأة فقال : تجتمع و تحتفر ( مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، ٤٣ المرأة كيف تكون في سجودھا ، ج اول ، ص ٢٤٢، نمبر ٢٧٧٨/٢٧٧٧/مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب تكبير المرأة بید بھا و قيام المرأة و رکوعھا و بجودها ، ج ثالث ، ص ٤٩ نمبر ٥٠٨٢) اس حدیث اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت سجدے کے اندر سکڑ کر رہے اور پیٹ کو رانوں سے ملا دے تاکہ زیادہ سے زیادہ ستر ہو سکے، یہی اسکے لئے بہتر ہے۔
ترجمه : (٤٦٨) اور دونوں سجدوں کے درمیان رانوں پر ہاتھ رکھ کر اطمینان سے بیٹھے۔
تشریح : جب دونوں سجدوں کے درمیان بیٹھے تو دونوں رانوں پر ہاتھوں کو رکھے، جیسے تشہد کے وقت رکھتے ہیں، اور پورے مطمئنا وسبّح فيه ثلاثا وجافي بطنه عن فخذيه وابدى عضديه (٤٧٠) ثم رفع رأسه مكبرا للنهوض اطمینان سے بیٹھے تا کہ تعدیل ارکان ہو جائے۔
وجه : (ا) فقال ابو حميد الساعدي .... فاذا جلس في الركعتين جلس على رجله اليسرى و نصب اليمنى واذا جلس في الركعة الآخرة قدم رجله اليسرى ونصب الاخرى وقعد على مقعدته ( بخاری شریف، باب سنۃ الجلوس في التشهد ، ص١٣٤، نمبر ٨٢٨ مسلم شریف ، باب ما تجمع صفته الصلوة وما ينفتح به ص ٢٠٥، نمبر ١١١٠/٤٩٨)
(٢) عن وائل بن حجر قال قدمت المدينة قلت لانظرن الى صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلما جلس یعنی للتشهد افترش رجله اليسرى ووضع يده اليسرى يعنى على فخذه اليسرى ونصب رجله اليمنى (ترمذی شریف، باب کیف الجلوس في التشهد ، ص ٧٩ ، نمبر ٢٩٢) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دائیں پاؤں کو کھڑا کیا اور بائیں کو بچھایا۔
ترجمه : (٤٦٩) پھر تکبیر کہے اور اطمینان سے دوسرا سجدہ کرے۔ اور اس میں کم سے کم تین مرتبہ تسبیح کہے۔ اور پیٹ کو رانوں سے علیحدہ رکھ کر بازو کو ظاہر کرے۔
تشریح : دوسرے سجدے میں بھی پہلے سجدے کی طرح اطمینان سے کرے، اور کم سے کم تین تسبیح کہے، اور پیٹ کو رانوں سے الگ رکھے ، اور بازو کو بھی الگ رکھے۔
ترجمه : (٤٧٠) پھر تکبیر کہتے ہوئے اٹھنے کے لئے سر اٹھائے زمین پر دونوں ہاتھوں سے سہارا دئے بغیر ، اور بیٹھے بغیر ۔
تشریح : دوسری رکعت کے لئے تکبیر کہتے ہوئے سر اٹھائے۔ اور پھر سیدھا کھڑا ہو اس طرح کہ نہ زمین پر بیٹھے اور نہ دونوں ہاتھوں سے زمین کو ٹیکے، بلکہ پاؤں کے بل سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے ، اس درمیان ران کا سہارا لے ۔ حنفیہ کے یہاں یہی سنت ہے لیکن اگر بڑھاپے یا کمزوری کی مجبوری ہو تو ہاتھ سے زمین کو ٹیک کر کھڑا ہوسکتا ہے۔
وجه : (١) حدیث یہ ہے عن ابي هريرة قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ينهض في الصلوة على صدور قدميه (ترمذی شریف، باب منه ايضا ( كيف النهوض من السجود ) ص ٧٨، نمبر ٢٨٨ رسنن للبیھقی ، باب من قال مرجع علی صدور قدمیہ، ج ثانی بص ١٧٩، نمبر ٢٧٦٣) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ بیٹھتے نہیں بلکہ پاؤں کے بل کھڑے ہو جاتے (٢) عن ابن عمر قال : نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم .... وقال ابن عبد الملک : نهى أن يعتمد الرجل على يديه اذا نهض في الصلوة (ابوداود شریف، باب كراهيته الاعتماد علی السید فی الصلوۃ ص ١٥١، نمبر ٩٩٢) اس حدیث میں تو اٹھتے وقت ٹیک لگانے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ (٣) أنه حديث محمد بن جحادة: اذا نهض نهض على ركبتيه واعتمد على فخذيه ۔ ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ١١٦ نمبر ٧٣٦ ) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ آپ سیدھے کھڑے ہو جاتے تھے۔ (٤) فحدثت به عطية العوفي فقال رأيت ابن عمر و ابن عباس ، و ابن الزبير ، و أبا سعيد الخدرى يقومون على صدور أقدامهم
Section on the composition of prayer. He keeps his armpits away in non-crowded conditions, directing the fingers of his hands and feet towards the qibla (467). And the woman lowers and sticks her belly to her thighs (468). And he sits between the two prostrations, placing his hands on his thighs, with tranquility (469). Then he says takbir and prostrates, and faces with the tips of his feet towards the qibla. (Bukhari...) From this hadith it is understood that in prostration the toes should be placed towards the qibla, and it also indicates that the fingers of the hands should also be towards the qibla. (4) In this hadith: from Aisha, she said: When the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated, he placed his hands facing the qibla. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) In this hadith, the Prophet used to place his hands towards the qibla. Glossary: armpit: kept away. Thigh: thigh. Upper arm: arm. Armpit: armpit. Crowd: crowd. Translation (467): And the woman lowers and sticks her belly to her thighs. Explanation: The woman prostrates lowering herself and sticks her belly to her thighs, because with regard to covering, this is better for her. Proof: (1) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... (2) From Ibn 'Umar... (3) From Ali... (4) From Ibn Abbas... From these hadith and athar, it is understood that the woman should contract in prostration and stick her belly to her thighs so that maximum covering is achieved, and this is better for her. Translation (468): And he sits between the two prostrations, placing his hands on his thighs, with tranquility. Explanation: When he sits between the two prostrations, he places his hands on both thighs, as he does in tashahhud, and fully with tranquility, and he glorifies three times in it, and he keeps his belly away from his thighs, and he exposes his upper arms (470). Then he raises his head saying takbir to stand up, he sits with tranquility so that the moderation of the pillars is achieved. Proof: (a) Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi said... (b) From Wa'il ibn Hujr... In this hadith, he erected his right foot and laid his left foot. Translation (469): Then he says takbir and performs the second prostration with tranquility. And in it he says the glorification at least three times. And he keeps his belly away from his thighs and exposes his arms. Explanation: In the second prostration, he does as in the first, with tranquility, and says at least three glorifications, keeps his belly away from his thighs, and also keeps his arms away. Translation (470): Then he raises his head saying takbir to stand up, without supporting himself on the ground with his hands, and without sitting. Explanation: He raises his head for the second rak'ah saying takbir. Then he stands straight such that he does not sit on the ground nor supports himself on the ground with his hands, rather he stands straight on his feet, supporting himself on his thighs in between. According to the Hanafis, this is the sunnah, but if due to old age or weakness there is necessity, he may support himself with his hands on the ground. Proof: (1) Hadith from Abu Hurairah... (2) From Ibn 'Umar: The Prophet forbade... (3) Hadith of Muhammad ibn Jahadah... (4) 'Atiyyah al-'Awfi said...
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (expansion) on the rulings of prostration posture and transitions in prayer. The text first addresses the general ruling for men: during prostration, the toes and fingers should face the qibla, and the armpits should be kept away from the sides (tajafi) when there is no crowding. The hadith from Bukhari and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah establish that the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed his hands facing the qibla, and the fingers of the feet should also face the qibla. The glossary explains key terms: jani (kept away), fakhdh (thigh), 'adud (upper arm), ibt (armpit), zuhmah (crowd).

Then the text moves to the women's ruling: a woman should lower herself in prostration and stick her belly to her thighs. The reason given is that it is more covering (satr). Proofs include multiple hadith: Abu Sa'id al-Khudri reports that the Prophet commanded men to keep their limbs apart in prostration and women to lower themselves; Ibn 'Umar reports the Prophet instructed women to stick their bellies to their thighs for maximum concealment; and athar from 'Ali and Ibn 'Abbas confirm that women should contract and keep close. These establish that women's prostration differs from men's in posture for modesty.

Next, the ruling on sitting between the two prostrations: one must sit with tranquility, placing hands on thighs. The text incorporates that in this sitting, one should glorify three times, keep the belly away from the thighs, and expose the upper arms (a part of the general tajafi for men). The proofs from Abu Humayd and Wa'il ibn Hujr detail the sitting posture: the left foot is laid flat, the right foot is erect, and hands are placed on thighs.

Then the second prostration: similar to the first, with tranquility, three tasbihat, belly away from thighs, arms exposed.

Finally, the rising from prostration for the second rak'ah: the head is raised with takbir, and one stands directly without sitting on the ground or using hands for support, instead rising on the soles of the feet. The Hanafi position is that this is the sunnah, but if one is elderly or weak, supporting with hands is permissible. Proofs include hadith from Abu Hurairah and Ibn 'Umar forbidding support on hands, and reports from companions rising on the soles of their feet.

Throughout, the passage emphasizes tranquility (itminan) and the distinction between men's and women's postures, particularly in prostration.

Key Terms
تجافي (tajafi): Keeping the limbs apart, especially in prostration, so that the belly is away from the thighs and the arms are not touching the ground.
اطمينان (itminan): Tranquility, pausing after each movement so that the body settles into position.
تسبيح (tasbih): Saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' (in prostration) or 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Adheem' (in ruku).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the sunnah prostration posture for a woman?
A) She should keep her belly away from her thighs like men.
B) She should lower herself and stick her belly to her thighs.
C) She should prostrate on her knees without bending.
D) She should raise her feet off the ground.

Key Takeaway
Men should keep limbs apart in prostration and rise without hand support; women should prostrate compactly; all are sunnah mu'akkadah based on hadith.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Position on Jalsah Istirahah: Direct Standing vs. Sitting Before Standing
Inter-madhhab dispute with dalil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing up from sajdah, identify the jalsah istirahah dispute, and explain the dalil and tarjih.

Core Idea
The Hanafi sunnah is to stand directly on the balls of the feet; jalsah istirahah is only for the excused.

After the second sajdah, the worshipper prepares to stand for the next rak'ah. The Hanafi school teaches that one should rise directly without sitting or using hand support—this is the sunnah. But Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a brief sitting (jalsah istirahah) is sunnah. This lesson unpacks the evidence and shows why the Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on standing after sajdah
Read the passage (470) and the explanation: standing without sitting or hand support is sunnah mu'akkadah. Note that support on the ground is only allowed for necessity.
This ruling is based on several hadith and practice of Companions.
2
Recognize the opposing Shafi'i position
The passage mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i considers jalsah istirahah (a brief sit before standing) as sunnah, with hand support. Read the 'fā'idah' section.
The Shafi'i evidence comes from the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Examine the four sources cited: hadith of Abu Huraira (rising on balls of feet), prohibition of hand support (Ibn Umar), practice of Companions, and the hadith of Muhammad ibn Jahadah. Understand how these prove the Hanafi position.
The Hanafi response interprets the Shafi'i hadith as applying only to odd rak'ahs or as a concession.
4
Understand the tarjih and practical difference
The Hanafi tarjih (preponderance) is that direct standing is the relied-upon position; jalsah istirahah is only permissible for the weak or elderly. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis do not perform the brief sit, while Shafi'is do in every rak'ah except the final.
This shows how a difference in dalil leads to a difference in practice.

ترجمه : (٤٧٠) پھر تکبیر کہتے ہوئے اٹھنے کے لئے سر اٹھائے زمین پر دونوں ہاتھوں سے سہارا دئے بغیر ، اور بیٹھے بغیر ۔ تشریح : دوسری رکعت کے لئے تکبیر کہتے ہوئے سر اٹھائے۔ اور پھر سیدھا کھڑا ہو اس طرح کہ نہ زمین پر بیٹھے اور نہ دونوں ہاتھوں سے زمین کو ٹیکے، بلکہ پاؤں کے بل سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے ، اس درمیان ران کا سہارا لے ۔ حنفیہ کے یہاں یہی سنت ہے لیکن اگر بڑھاپے یا کمزوری کی مجبوری ہو تو ہاتھ سے زمین کو ٹیک کر کھڑا ہوسکتا ہے۔

فائدة : امام شافعی کے یہاں یہ ہے کہ جلسہ استراحت کرے، یعنی تھوڑی دیر بیٹھے پھر زمین پر ٹیک لگا کر کھڑا ہو۔ ہمارے یہاں اس کی گنجائش بڑھاپے اور کمزوری کے وقت ہے۔
صل الله
وجه : (١) حدیث یہ ہے۔ اخبرنی مالک بن الحويرث الليثى انه رأى النبي عل يصلى فاذا كان في وتر من صلوته لم ينهض حتى يستوى قاعدا (بخاری شریف من استوی قاعدافی و تر من صلوته ثم نفض ، ص ١٣٣، نمبر ٨٢٣ ترمذی شریف ، باب کیف النحوض من السجود در ص ٧٨ نمبر ٧ (٢٨) (٢) جاء نا مالک بن الحويرث ... واذا رفع رأسه عن السجدة الثانية جلس واعتمد على الارض ثم قام ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب كيف يعتمد على الارض اذا قام من الركعة ،ص ١٣٣، نمبر ٨٢٤) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جلسہ استراحت سنت ہے۔
لغت : نهوض : کھڑا ہونا۔ اعتماد : ٹیک لگانا، اعتماد کرنا۔
Chapter on the Composition of Prayer. (469) Then he says the takbir and performs the second prostration with tranquility, and says subhanallah three times therein, and keeps his belly away from his thighs, and bares his arms. (470) Then he raises his head saying takbir for standing up, without supporting on the ground with his hands, and without sitting. Explanation: He raises his head for the second rak'ah saying takbir. Then he stands straight such that he does not sit on the ground nor support himself with his hands, but stands upright on his feet, taking support from his thighs in between. According to the Hanafis, this is the sunnah; but if there is necessity due to old age or weakness, he may stand by supporting his hands on the ground. Evidence: (1) Hadith from Abu Huraira: The Prophet used to rise in prayer on the balls of his feet. (2) Hadith from Ibn Umar: The Prophet forbade a man from supporting himself on his hands when rising in prayer. (3) Hadith of Muhammad bin Jahadah: When he rose, he rose on his knees and supported himself on his thighs. (4) Report from Atiyyah al-Awfi: He saw Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Zubayr, and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri rising on the balls of their feet without supporting on the ground with their hands and without sitting. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, one should perform jalsah istirahah (resting sitting), i.e., sit for a short while, then stand by supporting oneself on the ground. According to us, it is permissible only in old age or weakness. Evidence for the Shafi'i view: (1) Hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: He saw the Prophet pray, and when he was in an odd number of rak'ahs, he would not rise until he was sitting upright. (2) Hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: When he raised his head from the second prostration, he sat and supported himself on the ground, then stood. Vocabulary: nahawd: standing; i'timad: supporting.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with inter-madhhab dispute. It covers two rulings: the manner of the second prostration (number 469) and the manner of standing up for the second rak'ah (number 470). The second prostration requires tranquility, a minimum of three tashihs, and separating the belly from the thighs while keeping the arms away from the sides—these are sunnah acts. The standing up is done by rising directly on the balls of the feet without sitting first or using hand support, which is the Hanafi position based on multiple hadith and the practice of the Companions. The passage then presents the Shafi'i view that one should perform a brief sitting (jalsah istirahah) before standing, supporting the hands on the ground. The Hanafis respond by limiting this to cases of necessity, and they cite hadith that prohibit supporting on hands, reconciling the conflicting evidence by interpreting the Shafi'i hadith as referring to odd rak'ahs and applying the principle of istihsan for the weak. The ultimate Hanafi ruling is that the direct standing is sunnah mu'akkadah for those who are able, while jalsah istirahah is merely permissible for the elderly or ill.

Key Terms
جلسہ استراحت (jalsah istirahah): A brief sitting after the second prostration before standing for the next rak'ah.
نهوض (nuhud): Rising or standing up from prostration to the next rak'ah.
اعتماد (i'timad): Supporting oneself, especially with hands on the ground when standing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position regarding jalsah istirahah (resting sit) when standing for the next rak'ah?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah and should be performed by everyone.
B) It is permissible only for the elderly or those with a legitimate excuse.
C) It is obligatory and the prayer is invalid without it.
D) It is makruh tahrimi and should be avoided completely.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school emphasizes direct standing as sunnah mu'akkadah, with jalsah istirahah only as a concession for the excused.

Second Rak'ah: No Thana or Ta'awwudh
States that second rak'ah is identical except no thana or ta'awwudh, with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the difference between the first and second rak'ah regarding thana and ta'awwudh, and apply the Hanafi proof for omitting them in later rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Thana and ta'awwudh are sunnah only in the first rak'ah; they are never repeated.

The second rak'ah follows the first in all actions except two: the opening supplication (thana) and the seeking of refuge (ta'awwudh). This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling and the evidence that limits these recitations to the very beginning of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The omission of thana and ta'awwudh in the second rak'ah. Determine their legal status: sunnah, not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence for thana is the hadith of Aisha: 'When the Prophet began prayer, he said Subhanaka...' implying it is only at the start. For ta'awwudh, the practice of Hasan al-Basri shows it is recited once at the beginning.
Both proofs are zanni al-thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase in the hadith is 'when he began prayer' (اذا استفتح). This specifies the first moment, not later rak'ahs, indicating non-repetition.
Hanafi usul: limitation by indication of the sunnah.
4
Note the exception: basmalah
Unlike thana and ta'awwudh, basmalah is recited silently at the start of every rak'ah, based on hadith that the Prophet began every rak'ah with 'Bismillah'.
This shows continuity of basmalah across rak'ahs.
5
Recognize the Hanafi consistency
This ruling matches the Hanafi principle that thana and ta'awwudh are sunnah only at the beginning of the prayer, and not repeating them is the established practice (zahir al-riwayah).
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (٤٧١) اور دوسری رکعت پہلی جیسی ہے۔ ہاں اس میں ثنا اور اعوذ نہ پڑھے۔ تشریح : دوسری رکعت میں وہی اعمال کرے جو پہلی رکعت میں کئے ہیں۔ صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ پہلی رکعت میں ثناء یعنی سبحانک ، پڑھا اور اعوذ باللہ، یہاں یہ دونوں نہیں پڑھے گا۔
صل الله
وجه : (ا) عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله له اذا استفتح الصلوة قال سبحانک اللهم وبحمدک و تبارک اسمك و تعالى جدك ولا اله غیرک (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من رأی الاستفتاح بسجا تک ، ص ١٢١ نمبر ٧٧٦) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جب نماز شروع کرے تو سبحانک الخ پڑھے، اس لئے دوسری رکعت میں نہ پڑھے۔(٢)کان الحسن يستعيذ مرة حين يستفتح صلاته قبل ان يقرأ فاتحة الكتاب - مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب متى يستعيذ ، ج ثانی ص ٥٦، نمبر ٢٥٩٣) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ شروع میں اعوذ باللہ پڑھے۔ نوٹ : دوسری رکعت میں بسم اللہ آہستہ سے پڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ قرآت سے پہلے بسم اللہ آہستہ سے پڑھنا مسنون ہے۔(١) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان النبى الله يفتتح صلوته ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (ترمذی شریف، باب من رأی الجهر بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ص نمبر ٢٤٥) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر رکعت کو بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم سے شروع کرنا چاہئے (٢) عــــن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله لعل الله : اذا قرأتم الحمد لله فأقرءوا بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ، انها ام
Translation: (471) And the second rak'ah is like the first, except that he does not recite thana and ta'awwudh. Explanation: In the second rak'ah, he performs the same actions as in the first. The only difference is that in the first rak'ah he recited thana (subhanaka) and ta'awwudh (a'udhu billah); here he will not recite these two. Evidence: (1) 'A'isha narrated that when the Prophet began prayer he said: Subhanaka Allahumma... This hadith indicates that thana is recited at the beginning of the first rak'ah, so it is not recited in the second. (2) Hasan al-Basri used to recite ta'awwudh once when beginning his prayer before reciting Fatiha. This shows that ta'awwudh is only at the start. Note: In the second rak'ah, he will recite basmalah quietly, because reciting basmalah silently before recitation is sunnah. (1) Hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet began his prayer with 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' – indicating that every rak'ah should begin with basmalah. (2) Hadith from Abu Huraira: The Prophet said: When you recite al-hamdu lillah, then recite bismillah al-rahman al-rahim, for it is the mother...
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that the second rak'ah is identical to the first in all actions except two: the thana (subhanaka) and ta'awwudh (a'udhu billah) are not recited. These are opening supplications that are only said at the very beginning of the prayer. The evidence is from hadith where the Prophet recited thana only at the start of prayer, and the practice of Hasan al-Basri shows ta'awwudh is also once. Additionally, there is a note that basmalah should be recited silently at the beginning of every rak'ah, based on hadith that the Prophet began his prayer with basmalah and that every rak'ah should begin with it. The ruling is clear: the thana and ta'awwudh are not repeated in subsequent rak'ahs, but the basmalah is recited in each rak'ah before Fatiha.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): The opening supplication 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' recited at the start of prayer.
اعوذ بالله (ta'awwudh): The phrase 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' recited before Quran recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which rak'ah does a Hanafi recite thana (subhanaka) during salah?
A) In every rak'ah.
B) Only in the first rak'ah.
C) In the first and second rak'ahs.
D) Only in the final rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
The second rak'ah is identical to the first except thana and ta'awwudh are omitted; these are sunnah only at the beginning of the prayer.

The Second Rak'ah and the Sitting of Rest (Jalsat al-Istirahah)
Ruling on second rak'ah and inter-madhhab dispute on sitting of rest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school omits thana' and ta'awwudh in the second rak'ah and evaluate the Shafi'i argument for jalsat al-istirahah.

Core Idea
The second rak'ah repeats the first except thana' and ta'awwudh; jalsat al-istirahah is a concession, not a sunnah.

This passage addresses two distinct but related points: the structure of the second rak'ah and the disputed sitting of rest (jalsat al-istirahah). The author begins by establishing the Hanafi ruling that the second rak'ah is identical to the first except for the opening supplications, which are only recited at the very beginning of prayer. He then presents the Shafi'i view that a brief sitting between prostrations is sunnah, and clarifies the Hanafi response: this sitting is only a concession for the elderly or weak. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly performing the prayer according to the Hanafi school and appreciating how different schools derive rulings from the same hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the second rak'ah
The text states: 'The second rak'ah is like the first except that he does not recite thana' nor ta'awwudh.' Identify which actions are carried over and which are omitted.
Thana' and ta'awwudh are sunnah only at the start of the entire prayer, not per rak'ah.
2
Locate the evidence for omitting thana' and ta'awwudh
The passage cites a hadith from Aisha that the Prophet would recite 'Subhanaka Allahumma' when opening the prayer (not per rak'ah), and a statement from Hasan al-Basri that he would seek refuge only at the beginning.
3
Examine the Shafi'i position on jalsat al-istirahah
The fa'idah says that according to Imam al-Shafi'i, one should sit briefly after the second prostration before rising, relying on the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith.
The Shafi'i consider this sitting a sunnah of the prayer.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response interprets the same hadith as a concession for the elderly or weak, noting that the general practice of the Companions was to rise directly without sitting.
The Hanafi position is thus that jalsat al-istirahah is not sunnah but only permissible when needed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a healthy Hanafi worshipper rises directly from prostration without sitting; a Shafi'i worshipper sits briefly before standing. Each is valid within its school.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute combined with a ruling statement. The author (likely a Hanafi scholar) begins by stating the ruling (471): the second rak'ah is identical to the first in all actions except that thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma) and ta'awwudh (A'udhu billah) are not recited. The reason is that thana' is a sunnah opening supplication performed only at the beginning of the prayer, and ta'awwudh is also only at the start. The author then provides a fa'idah (benefit) addressing the Shafi'i view on jalsat al-istirahah (sitting briefly between prostrations). The Shafi'i school considers it sunnah to sit momentarily after the second prostration before rising for the next rak'ah. The Hanafi school, however, holds that this sitting is only permissible for the elderly or weak, and the normal practice is to rise directly using the hands for support on the knees. The author supports the Hanafi position with hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith showing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would sit before rising in odd-numbered rak'ahs. The commentary explains that the second rak'ah is exactly like the first in its obligations and sunan, except the opening supplications. A note adds that Bismillah should still be recited silently in the second rak'ah, as it is sunnah before recitation in every rak'ah.

Key Terms
ثناء (thanā'): The opening supplication 'Subhanaka Allahumma' recited at the beginning of the first rak'ah.
اعوذ (a'udhū): The phrase 'A'udhu billahi min ash-shaytan ir-rajim' seeking refuge in Allah.
جلسة استراحة (jalsat al-istirāḥah): A brief sitting after the second prostration before rising for the next rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
The second rak'ah mirrors the first except for the opening supplications; jalsat al-istirahah is a concession, not a sunnah, in the Hanafi school.

Seven Places for Raising Hands in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on specific occasions for raising hands in prayer and worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven (or more) specific occasions for raising hands in Hanafi fiqh and explain the proof for each.

Core Idea
Raising hands is sunnah only in seven specific situations—not at every posture change.

This passage from Thamarat al-Najah details the Hanafi position on raf' al-yadayn, clarifying exactly when the worshipper raises hands. While many Muslims raise hands at every change of posture (ruku, sujud, etc.), the Hanafi school restricts it to takbirat al-ihram, the qunut of witr, the extra takbirs of 'Id, and a few other places outside the prayer. The passage also provides the evidence from the Companion Ibn 'Abbas and the Quranic verse commanding stillness in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling statement
Read the opening phrase 'ولا يسنّ رفع اليدين' and note that the default is that raising hands is not sunnah except where specified.
The list includes both actions inside salah (takbirat al-ihram, witr qunut, 'id takbirs) and outside salah (seeing Ka'bah, etc.).
2
List the seven places
From the text, enumerate the occasions: (1) at the beginning of every prayer, (2) at the takbir of qunut in witr, (3) at the extra takbirs of 'Id, (4) when seeing the Ka'bah, (5) when kissing the Black Stone, (6) when standing on Safa and Marwah, (7) when standing at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah, (8) after throwing the first and middle jamrah, (9) when making supplication after prayers (tasbih). Note that the author considers some as one category.
The text actually lists nine items, but the Companion narration mentions seven; the commentator reconciles them.
3
Distinguish inside vs. outside salah
Note that only three of the occasions occur during the prayer (takbirat al-ihram, witr qunut, 'id takbirs). The rest are outside the formal prayer, such as during Hajj or when seeing the Ka'bah.
This helps avoid the misconception that Hanafis raise hands in every rak'ah.
4
Examine the proofs
The text cites the statement of Ibn 'Abbas (a companion) listing seven places, and another hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) mentioning raising hands at those places. It also refers to Quran 2:238 'Qumoo lillahi qaniteen' to argue that prayer requires stillness, so hands are not raised repeatedly.
The Hanafi position relies on the understanding that the command for devotion implies minimal movement.
5
Compare with other schools
Note that the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools consider raising hands sunnah at every change of posture (ruku, rising, etc.). The Maliki school also limits it to takbirat al-ihram but differs on some details.
The difference stems from the interpretation of the evidence: the Hanafis prioritize the companion's practice and the general command of stillness.

Fruit of Success Volume 1 313 Section on the Composition of Prayer He seeks refuge (472. alif) And it is not sunnah to raise the hands except at the beginning of every prayer, and at the takbir of qunut in witr, and the extra takbirs of the two 'ids, and when one sees the Ka'bah, and when one kisses the Black Stone, and when one stands on Safa and Marwah, and when standing at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah, and after throwing the first and middle jamrah, and at the time of tasbih after prayers ... Translation: (472 [alif]) And it is not sunnah to raise the hands except at the beginning of every prayer, and in witr the takbir of qunut, and the extra takbirs of the two 'ids, and when seeing the Ka'bah, and when kissing the Black Stone, and when standing on Safa and Marwah, and when standing at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah, and after throwing the first and middle jamrah, and after prayers at the time of tasbih [i.e., when supplicating]. Explanation: The author means that raising the hands at every rak'ah when going into ruku, rising from ruku, going into sujud, and rising for the second rak'ah is not sunnah according to the Hanafis. Only at takbirat al-ihram is raising the hands to the ears sunnah. Additionally, raising hands is sunnah at takbirat al-ihram, the extra takbirs of 'id, and the qunut supplication in witr. The remaining six places are outside of prayer. The total are: ... Proof: (1) The evidence for raising hands in these seven places is the statement of the Companion: Ibn 'Abbas said: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places: when standing for prayer, when seeing the House (Ka'bah), on Safa, on Marwah, at 'Arafat, at Muzdalifah (Jam'), and at the jamarat.' ... (2) From Ibn 'Abbas from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Hands are raised in prayer, when seeing the House, on Safa and Marwah, on the evening of 'Arafah, at Muzdalifah, at the two jamrahs, and over the deceased.' ... Basis: The main point is that Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa) looked at the verse 'Stand before Allah in devotion' (2:238) ...
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the specific occasions for raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by stating the ruling (472): raising the hands is not sunnah except in seven specific places. These are: (1) at the beginning of every prayer (takbirat al-ihram), (2) at the takbir for qunut in witr, (3) at the extra takbirs of the two 'Id prayers, (4) when seeing the Ka'bah, (5) when kissing the Black Stone, (6) when standing on Safa and Marwah, (7) when standing at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah, (8) after throwing the first and middle jamrah (this makes eight, but the author considers some as one). Actually, the list in the translation includes nine items. The commentary (tashrih) clarifies that within salah, raising hands is only sunnah at takbirat al-ihram, the qunut takbir in witr, and the extra takbirs in 'id prayers. The other places (seeing Ka'bah, etc.) are outside salah. The author then provides proofs from hadith: the narration of Ibn 'Abbas listing seven places, and another hadith from the same Companion. The core Hanafi position is based on the verse 'Qumoo lillahi qaniteen' (2:238), which implies stillness in prayer, thus avoiding excessive movements like raising hands repeatedly. This is a distinctive feature of the Hanafi school compared to others who raise hands at every change of posture.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands up to the ears or shoulders during prayer, done at specific times.
تكبير القنوت (takbīr al-qunūt): The takbir said when raising hands for the qunut supplication in the witr prayer.
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbīrāt al-zawā'id): The extra takbirs recited in the 'Id prayer (three in first rak'ah, three in second besides takbirat al-ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which of the following situations is it sunnah to raise the hands?
A) When going into ruku' in each rak'ah.
B) When rising from ruku' in each rak'ah.
C) At the takbir for qunut in witr prayer.
D) When prostrating in each rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
Raising hands is a confirmed sunnah only in seven specific situations, not during every change of posture in prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Occasions for Raising Hands (Raf' al-Yadayn) in Hanafi Fiqh
List of occasions for raising hands with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific occasions where raising hands is sunnah according to the Hanafi school and cite the primary hadith proofs that form the basis of this position.

Core Idea
Raising hands during prayer is sunnah only at the opening takbir and a few occasions – the Prophet never raised at ruku' or sujud.

This passage from a classical Hanafi fiqh text clarifies a common point of confusion: when exactly should a Hanafi raise his hands in prayer? Many Muslims from other schools raise hands at every movement, but the Hanafi school restricts it to specific moments both inside and outside prayer. We will examine the listed occasions, the hadith proofs, and the underlying principle of stillness (sukun) that governs the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the occasions inside prayer
From the passage, extract the three occasions inside the prayer itself: the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah), the takbir of qunut in witr, and the additional takbirs of the Eid prayers.
These are the only times hands are raised during the actual prayer according to Hanafis.
2
Identify the occasions outside prayer
The passage then lists six occasions outside prayer: seeing the Kaaba, touching the Black Stone, standing on Safa and Marwah, standing at Arafah and Muzdalifah, after throwing the first and middle Jamarat, and when making supplication after prayers.
These are based on the saying of Ibn Abbas and a hadith from the Prophet.
3
Analyze the primary hadith proofs
The passage cites four key hadiths: Ibn Mas'ud (Tirmidhi) – prayed without raising except the first time; al-Bara' (Abu Dawud) – raised only at opening; Jabir ibn Samurah (Muslim) – commanded stillness, implicitly prohibiting repeated raising; 'Alqamah (Darqutni) – practice of Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar was to raise only at the first takbir.
Each hadith emphasizes that the Prophet and the early caliphs did not raise hands at ruku' or other movements.
4
Understand the principle of stillness (sukun)
The author links the Hanafi position to the Quranic verse 'Stand for Allah in devotion' (2:238) and the hadith commanding calmness in prayer. Repeated hand-raising disturbs the required tranquility.
This is the legal 'illa (reason) behind restricting raf' al-yadayn.
5
Recognize the ikhtilaf and the Hanafi tarjih
The Shafi'i school uses the hadith of Ibn Umar to justify raising at ruku' and rising. The Hanafis respond by interpreting that hadith as referring to the opening takbir and by preferring the specific hadiths that show the contrary practice. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Hanafi view.
The practical difference is that Hanafis do not raise at ruku', while Shafi'is do.

فصل في تركيب الصلوة
يتعوّذ ( ۴۷۲. الف) ولا يسنّ رفع اليدين الا عند افتتاح كل صلوة وعند تكبير القنوت في الوتر وتكبيرات الزوائد في العيدين وحين يرى الكعبة وحين يستلم الحجر الاسود وحين يقوم على الصفا والمروة وعند الوقوف بعرفة ومزدلفة وبعد رمي الجمرة الاولى والوسطى وعند التسبيح عقب القرآن و أم الكتاب و السبع المثاني ، و بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم احداها - ( دار قطنی باب وجوب قراءة بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم في الصلوۃ ، ج اول ص ۳۱۰ نمبر ۱۱۷۷) اس حدیث میں تاکید ہے کہ جب جب الحمد پڑھے تو بسم اللہ پڑھے اسلئے بسم اللہ ہر رکعت میں آہستہ پڑھے۔

والمرأة کہ نماز میں سکون سے کھڑے رہو اور بار بار ہاتھ اٹھا نا سکون کے خلاف ہے اسلئے اس احادیث پر عمل کیا۔ حدیث یہ ہے (۲) قال عبد الله بن مسعود الا اصلي بكم صلوة رسول الله فصلى فلم يرفع يديه الا في اول مرة . (ترمذی شریف، باب ان النبی لم يرفع الا في اول مرة، ص، نمبر ۲۵۷) (۳) عن البراء ان رسول الله كان اذا افتتح الصلوة رفع يديه الى قريب من اذنيه ثم لا يعود . (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من لم يذكر الرفع عند الركوع ، ص ۱۱۸، نمبر ۷۴۹ و نسائی شریف ، باب رفع الیدین و ترك الملكين عند الرفع من الركوع والرخصة في ترك ذلك ص ۱۲۰، نمبر ۱۰۵۹) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رکوع کے وقت ہاتھ نہیں اٹھاتے تھے۔ (۴) عن جابر بن سمرة قال: خرج علينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال مالی اراکم رافعی ايديكم كانها اذ ناب خيل شمس؟ اسكنوا في الصلوة (مسلم شریف ، باب الامر بالسكون في الصلوة والنهي عن الاشارة باليد، ص ۱۸۳ نمبر ۹۶۸/۴۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں سکون اور اطمینان مطلوب ہے ۔ اور بار بار ہاتھ اٹھانے میں سکون نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بھی رفع یدین نہیں ہونا چاہئے (۵) عن علقمة عن عبد الله قال صليت مع النبي ومع ابي بكر و مع عمر فلم يرفع ايديهم الا عند التكبيرة الاولى في افتتاح الصلوة (دار قطنی ، باب ذكر التکبیر ورفع الیدین الخ ، ج اول ص ۲۹۶ نمبر ۱۱۲۰ و ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء ان النبي لم يرفع الا في اول مرة ، ج اول ص، نمبر ۲۵۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر اولی کے علاوہ کسی وقت بھی رفع یدین نہیں کرنا چاہئے۔
Section on the construction of prayer. He seeks refuge (472 [a]) and it is not sunnah to raise the hands except at the beginning of every prayer, and at the takbir of qunut in witr, and the additional takbirs in the two Eids, and when he sees the Kaaba, and when he touches the Black Stone, and when he stands on Safa and Marwah, and at standing at Arafah and Muzdalifah, and after throwing the first and middle Jamarat, and at the tasbih after the Qur'an and Umm al-Kitab and the Seven Oft-Repeated [verses], and 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' is one of them. (Darqutni, chapter on the obligation of reciting Bismillah in prayer, vol. 1, p. 310, no. 1177) This hadith emphasizes that whenever he recites Al-Hamd, he should recite Bismillah, so he should recite Bismillah softly in every rak'ah.
Translation (472 [a]): And it is not sunnah to raise the hands except when beginning every prayer, and at the takbir of qunut in witr, and the additional takbirs of the two Eids, and when seeing the Kaaba, and when kissing the Black Stone, and when standing on Safa and Marwah, and at standing in Arafah and Muzdalifah, and after throwing the first and middle Jamarat, and at the time of tasbih after prayers [i.e., when supplicating]. Explanation: The author intends to say that raising the hands when going into ruku', rising from ruku', going into sujud, and rising for the second rak'ah is not sunnah according to the Hanafis; it is only sunnah to raise the hands to the ears at the time of the takbir tahrimah. And besides that, raising the hands to the ears is sunnah at the takbir tahrimah, at the additional takbirs in the two Eids, and at the qunut supplication in witr. The remaining six places are outside prayer. The total are: (4) when seeing the Kaaba, (5) when kissing the Black Stone, (6) when standing on Safa and Marwah, (7) at standing in Arafah and Muzdalifah, (8) after throwing the first and middle Jamarat, (9) at the time of supplication after prayers. Proof: (1) The evidence for raising the hands in these seven places is the saying of a Companion: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'Do not raise the hands except in seven places: when standing for prayer, when seeing the House, on Safa, on Marwah, in Arafat, in Muzdalifah, and at the Jamarat.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on 'Who used to raise his hands at the first takbir and then not repeat' vol. 1, p. 214, no. 2450) This Companion's saying indicates that the hands should be raised at the takbir in seven places, which do not include ruku'. (2) From Ibn Abbas from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'The hands are raised in prayer, when seeing the House, on Safa and Marwah, on the evening of Arafah, at the two Jamarat, and over the deceased.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on raising hands when seeing the House, vol. 5, p. 117, no. 9210) This hadith indicates that the hands should be raised at the takbir in seven places, which do not include ruku'. Proof: (1) The original matter is that Imam A'zam's gaze is on the verse 'Stand for Allah in devotion' (Quran 2:238). And the woman: that in prayer she should stand calmly, and repeatedly raising the hands is against calmness, therefore he acted on these hadiths. The hadith are: (2) Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'Should I not pray with you the prayer of the Messenger of Allah?' So he prayed and did not raise his hands except the first time. (Tirmidhi, chapter on the Prophet not raising except the first time, p. no. 257) (3) From al-Bara': That the Messenger of Allah, when he began prayer, raised his hands close to his ears, then did not return. (Abu Dawud, chapter on 'Who did not mention raising at ruku'', p. 118, no. 749; Nasa'i, chapter on raising hands and the omission of the two angels at raising from ruku' and the permission to leave that, p. 120, no. 1059) From these hadiths, it is known that he did not raise his hands at the time of ruku'. (4) From Jabir ibn Samurah, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah came out to us and said: 'Why do I see you raising your hands as if they are the tails of restive horses? Be calm in prayer.' (Muslim, chapter on the command to be calm in prayer and the prohibition of gesturing with the hand, p. 183, no. 968/430) From this hadith, it is known that calmness and tranquility are required in prayer, and repeatedly raising the hands lacks tranquility. For this reason, raising the hands should not be done. (5) From 'Alqamah from 'Abdullah, he said: 'I prayed with the Prophet, with Abu Bakr, and with 'Umar, and they did not raise their hands except at the first takbir in the opening of prayer.' (Darqutni, chapter on mentioning the takbir and raising hands, vol. 1, p. 296, no. 1120; Tirmidhi, chapter on what is narrated that the Prophet did not raise except the first time, vol. 1, p. no. 257) From this hadith, it is known that one should not raise the hands at any time except the first takbir.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling-with-proof on the Hanafi position regarding raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) during and outside prayer. The author begins by listing the specific occasions where raising the hands is sunnah: (1) at the opening takbir of every prayer, (2) at the qunut takbir in witr, (3) at the additional takbirs in Eid prayers, and then six occasions outside prayer: seeing the Kaaba, touching the Black Stone, standing on Safa and Marwah, standing at Arafah and Muzdalifah, after throwing the first and middle Jamarat, and when making supplication after prayers (the 'tasbih' here refers to dua). The translation clarifies that the original statement in Arabic means that raising hands is not sunnah except at these specified times. The explanation emphasizes that, contrary to the practice of some other schools, the Hanafis do not raise hands when going into ruku', rising from ruku', going into sujud, or standing up for the next rak'ah. The sunnah is only at the takbir tahrimah (opening takbir) and at the qunut and Eid takbirs. The rest of the seven occasions are outside the prayer. The author then provides proofs: first, the saying of Ibn Abbas that hands are raised in seven places (which exclude ruku'). Then a hadith from the Prophet listing similar places. To support the non-raising during ruku', the author cites the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud who prayed without raising except the first time, and the hadith of al-Bara' that the Prophet raised only at the opening. The hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah emphasizes stillness in prayer, which repeated hand-raising would disturb. Finally, the hadith of 'Alqamah confirms that the practice of the Prophet and the first two caliphs was to raise only at the first takbir. The underlying principle, the author notes, is based on the Quranic command 'Stand for Allah in devotion' (2:238), which implies stillness and solemnity. The text defends the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i practice of raising at every movement, though the debate is not explicitly named. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that the sunnah is to raise the hands only at the opening takbir and at the specified occasions. This is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising both hands up to the ears or shoulders, typically during takbir in prayer.
مسنون (masnun): A recommended act based on the practice of the Prophet (sunnah).
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in the witr prayer, for which hands are raised.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, at which of the following is raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) considered sunnah?
A) When going into ruku'
B) When rising from ruku'
C) At the opening takbir of prayer
D) During every movement in prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts raf' al-yadayn to the opening takbir and a few specific occasions, based on hadith and the principle of stillness in prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Posture of Sitting (Jalsah) in the Second Rak'ah for Men
Ruling on the sitting posture after the second sajdah in prayer for men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah posture for a man in the first tashahhud and identify the supporting hadith evidence from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi and Wa'il ibn Hujr.

Core Idea
The sunnah posture for sitting in the first tashahhud is iftirash: sit on the left foot with the right foot erect.

This lesson details the specific posture (jalsah) recommended for men during the second rak'ah of prayer, specifically for the tashahhud. The Hanafi school, relying on authentic hadith from the Prophet's practice, prescribes sitting on the left foot while keeping the right foot upright with toes towards the qibla. Understanding this sunnah helps perfect one's prayer and follow the Prophetic example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exact action is being ruled upon? The act is the sitting posture after the second sajdah in the second rak'ah. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof comes from hadith: Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi (Bukhari, Muslim) and Wa'il ibn Hujr (Tirmidhi). These describe the Prophet's sitting posture.
Both are ahad hadith, zanni in transmission and meaning, but sufficient for sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit description of the Prophet's actions in these hadiths is taken as the sunnah practice to be emulated. The command 'pray as you have seen me pray' supports following this posture.
The Hadith of Abu Humayd distinguishes between first and final tashahhud.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no major inter-madhhab dispute on this specific posture for the second rak'ah; it is mostly agreed upon. Some may use different postures, but the Hanafi rely on these hadith.
The Shafi'i school also uses iftirash for the first tashahhud.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a man should spread his left foot, sit on it, erect the right foot, point toes to qibla, and place hands on thighs with fingers spread.
This is for the first tashahhud; the final tashahhud uses tawarruk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۷۲ [ب]) اور جب مرد دوسری رکعت کے سجدے سے فارغ ہو تو اپنا بایاں پاؤں بچھائے اور اس پر بیٹھے اور داہنا پاؤں کھڑا رکھے اور انگلیوں کو قبلہ رو کرے اور ہاتھوں کو رانوں پر انگلیاں پھیلا کر رکھے۔
وجه : (ا) فقال ابو حميد الساعدي .... فاذا جلس في الركعتين جلس على رجله اليسرى و نصب اليمني واذا جلس في الركعة الآخرة قدم رجله اليسرى ونصب الاخرى وقعد على مقعدته ( بخاری شریف، باب سنۃ الجلوس في التشهد، ص۱۳۴، نمبر ۸۲۸ مسلم شریف ، باب ما تجمع صفة الصلوة وما تفتح به، ص ۲۰۵، نمبر ۸ ۱۰/۴۹) (۲) عن وائـل بـن حـجـر قـال قـدمـت المدينة قلت لانظرن الى صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلما جلس ـ یعنی للتشهد ـ افترش رجله اليسرى ووضع يده اليسرى يعنى على فخذه اليسرى ونصب رجله الیمنی (ترمذی شریف ، باب کیف الجلوس في التشهد ، ص ۷۹، نمبر ۲۹۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دائیں پاؤں کو کھڑا کیا اور بائیں کو بچھایا۔ اور یہ بھی ہے کہ ہاتھوں کو ران پر رکھے (۳) انگلیاں قبلہ کی طرف رکھے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔قال اجتمع ابو حميد الساعدی .... قال ابـو حـمـيـد انـا اعـلـمـكـم بصلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكر الحديث قال فيه ثم جلس فافترش رجله
Translation (472 [b]): And when the man finishes the prostrations of the second rak'ah, he should spread his left foot and sit on it, and keep his right foot upright, and turn its toes towards the qibla, and place his hands on his thighs with fingers spread. Proof: (a) Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi said: 'When he sat in the two rak'ahs, he sat on his left foot and erected the right one, and when he sat in the final rak'ah, he moved forward his left foot and erected the other and sat on his buttocks.' (Bukhari, chapter on the sunnah of sitting in tashahhud, p. 134, no. 828; Muslim, chapter on the description of prayer and its opening, p. 205, no. 810/49) (2) From Wa'il ibn Hujr, he said: 'I came to Medina and said, I will certainly observe the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. When he sat – meaning for tashahhud – he spread his left foot and placed his left hand on his left thigh, and erected his right foot.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on how to sit in tashahhud, p. 79, no. 292) This hadith mentions that he erected the right foot and spread the left, and also that he placed his hands on his thighs. (3) He turns his fingers towards the qibla; the evidence for this is the hadith: Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi gathered... and Abu Humayd said: 'I am the most knowledgeable among you of the prayer of the Messenger of Allah.' He related the hadith and said: 'Then he sat and spread his foot.'
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on the posture of sitting (jalsah) in the second rak'ah of prayer, specifically for men. The text begins with the ruling: after the second sajdah of the second rak'ah, the man should sit on his left foot, keeping his right foot upright with the toes pointing towards the qibla. His hands are placed on his thighs with fingers spread. This is described as the sunnah posture for the tashahhud in the second rak'ah. The text then gives the proofs: the hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi, which describes the Prophet's sitting in the two rak'ahs (i.e., the first tashahhud) as sitting on the left foot with the right foot erect. Another hadith from Wa'il ibn Hujr also confirms spreading the left foot and erecting the right. A third hadith indicates that the toes should face the qibla. The mention of 'fingers spread' (بسط اصابعه) is understood to be with the palms on the thighs, fingers extended naturally. The passage is a straightforward ruling with proof, aimed at teaching the correct sunnah posture. The Hanafi view is that this posture is for the first tashahhud (in a 3 or 4 rak'ah prayer) and is also applicable for the second tashahhud with slight modifications (the final tashahhud is different). The text does not discuss the woman's posture, but later sections (in other parts of the book) address it. For now, the ruling applies to men.

Key Terms
افتراش (iftirash): The action of spreading the left foot and sitting on it, with the right foot erect.
نصب (nasb): Erecting or raising the right foot vertically, with toes pointing to qibla.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited while sitting in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first tashahhud of a four-rak'ah prayer, what is the sunnah posture for a man according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sitting on both feet with the right foot tucked
B) Sitting on the left foot with the right foot erect and toes pointing to qibla
C) Sitting cross-legged
D) Kneeling with both knees on the ground

Key Takeaway
The sunnah posture for the first tashahhud in prayer for a man is iftirash: sit on the left foot with the right foot erect and toes towards the qibla.

Salah — Prayer

Hanafi Proof for Not Raising Hands During Prayer
Hadith evidence for Hanafi stance on raf' al-yadayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on raf' al-yadayn and explain the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
The Prophet raised his hands only at the first takbir; stillness in prayer is commanded.

The issue of raising hands during prayer (raf' al-yadayn) is a well-known point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. Classical Hanafi texts present multiple hadiths showing that the Prophet ﷺ and the Rightly Guided Caliphs did not raise their hands after the opening takbir. In this lesson, we examine the primary proofs from the Sunnah that establish the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon: raising hands at which points? The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah to raise hands only at the opening takbir; at other takbirs it is not sunnah.
The act is raf' al-yadayn (raising hands) at takbirs other than the opening.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites five hadiths from various sources. Identify each hadith and its general meaning.
Hadiths are from Ibn Mas'ud, al-Bara', Jabir ibn Samurah, and 'Alqamah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each hadith prove the ruling? For example, hadith of Ibn Mas'ud shows the Prophet did not raise after the first takbir; the command 'Be still' in Jabir's hadith prohibits unnecessary movement.
The imperative 'اسكنوا' indicates obligation to remain still.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that raising hands at every takbir is sunnah, based on hadiths showing the Prophet raising at ruku' and after rising.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each school has its proofs.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school prefers the hadiths of action over those of speech, and the practice of the caliphs is given weight. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to raise only at the opening takbir.
Tarjih authority: Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في تركيب الصلوة
الصلوة ( ۴۷۲. ب) واذا فرغ الرجل من سجدتى الركعة الثانية افترش رجله اليسرى وجلس عليها ونـصـب يـمـنــاه ووجه اصابعها نحو القبلة ووضع يديه على فخذيه وبسط اصابعه (۴۷۳) والمرأة کہ نماز میں سکون سے کھڑے رہو اور بار بار ہاتھ اٹھا نا سکون کے خلاف ہے اس لئے اس احادیث پر عمل کیا۔ حدیث یہ ہے (۲) قال صلى الله عبد الله بن مسعود الا اصلي بكم صلوة رسول الله لا فصلى فلم يرفع يديه الا في اول مرة . (ترندی شریف، باب ان النبی تم یرفع الا فی اول مرة ، ص، اے نمبر ۲۵۷) (۳) عن البراء ان رسول الله له كان اذا افتتح الصلوة رفع يديه الى قريب من اذنيه ثم لا يعود . (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من لم یذکر الرفع عند الرکوع ، ص ۱۱۸، نمبر ۷۴۹ نسائی شریف ، باب رفع الیدین خذ و الملكين عند الرفع من الركوع والرخصة في ترک ذلک ص ۱۲۰، نمبر ۱۰۵۹) ان احادیث سے صلى الله معلوم ہوا کہ رکوع کے وقت ہاتھ نہیں اٹھاتے تھے۔ (۴) عن جابر بن سمرة قال: خرج علينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال مالی اراکم رافعی ايديكم كانها اذ ناب خيل شمس؟ اسكنوا في الصلوة (مسلم شریف ، باب الامر بالسكون في الصلوة والنهي عن الاشارة باليد، ص ۱۸۳ نمبر ۹۶۸/۴۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں سکون اور اطمینان مطلوب ہے ۔ اور صلى الله بار بار ہاتھ اٹھانے میں سکون نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بھی رفع یدین نہیں ہونا چاہئے (۵) عن علقمة عن عبد الله قال صليت مع النبي عل ومع ابي بكر و مع عمر فلم يرفع ايديهم الا عند التكبيرة الاولى في افتتاح الصلوة (دار قطنی ، باب ذكر التکبیر ورفع الیدین الخ ، ج اول ص ۲۹۶ نمبر ۱۱۲۰ر ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء ان النبي الله لم يرفع الا في اول مرة ، ج اول ی اے، نمبر ۲۵۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر اولی کے علاوہ کسی وقت بھی رفع یدین نہیں کرنا چاہئے۔
Chapter on the composition of prayer. Prayer (472b) And when the man finishes the two prostrations of the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot and sits on it, and erects his right foot and directs its toes toward the qibla, and places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers. (473) And the woman: stand in prayer with tranquility, and repeatedly raising hands is against tranquility, so he acted upon these hadiths. Hadith it is: (2) 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'Shall I not pray with you the prayer of the Messenger of Allah?' So he prayed and did not raise his hands except at the first time. (3) From al-Bara': that the Messenger of Allah, when he opened the prayer, raised his hands near his ears then did not return. From these hadiths it is known that he did not raise his hands at the time of ruku'. (4) From Jabir ibn Samurah: he said: 'The Messenger of Allah came out to us and said: Why do I see you raising your hands as if they are tails of restless horses? Be still in prayer.' From this hadith it is known that tranquility and calmness are required in prayer, and repeatedly raising hands does not have tranquility. Therefore, raf' al-yadayn should not be done. (5) From 'Alqamah from 'Abdullah: he said: 'I prayed with the Prophet, and with Abu Bakr, and with 'Umar, and they did not raise their hands except at the first takbir at the opening of the prayer.' From this hadith it is known that raf' al-yadayn should not be done at any time except the first takbir.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a proof section for the Hanafi position that the hands should not be raised during prayer except at the initial takbir (takbirat al-ihram). The author presents five hadiths. The first two (from Ibn Mas'ud and al-Bara') show that the Prophet did not raise his hands after the opening takbir. The third (from Jabir) emphasizes stillness in prayer, implying that raising hands disrupts tranquility. The fourth (from 'Alqamah) states that the caliphs also did not raise hands except at the beginning. These are core Hanafi proofs against the Shafi'i practice of raising hands at every movement. The Hanafi school relies on these as authentic (sahih) and considers the practice of not raising hands as the sunnah. The ruling is that raf' al-yadayn is not sunnah except at the opening takbir.

Key Terms
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer, specifically at the takbirs for bowing, standing, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah, what did the Prophet command?
A) Raise your hands
B) Be still in prayer
C) Lower your hands
D) Make the takbir louder

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi proof for not raising hands is based on explicit actions of the Prophet and the command to remain still in prayer, establishing that the sunnah is to raise only at the opening takbir.

Women's Tawarruk in Tashahhud
Ruling on women's sitting in tashahhud with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the manner of women's tawarruk in tashahhud according to the Hanafi school and cite the supporting evidences.

Core Idea
Women sit on left buttock (tawarruk) with both feet to the right in tashahhud for modesty and ease.

This passage addresses a specific ruling within the prayer: how a woman should sit during the recitation of tashahhud. While the general sitting (tawarruk) is known for men in the final sitting, the Hanafi school prescribes a modified form for women based on considerations of modesty (sitr) and ease. The text presents multiple prophetic hadith and an athar from the Companion 'Ata' to support this differentiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the recommended sitting for a woman in tashahhud is: it is tawarruk, i.e., sitting on the left buttock with both feet placed to the right side.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi in Abu Dawood and Muslim describes the Prophet's tawarruk in the final sitting. The Hanafi school applies this specifically to women by analogy and based on other evidences.
The hadith uses the phrase 'qada mutawarrikan 'ala shiqihi al-aysar'.
3
Examine the supporting evidences
The Bukhari version and the athar from 'Ata' confirm that a woman sits on her left side, and it is acceptable to adopt the easiest manner that achieves gathering.
The athar explicitly states that the left side is preferred for women.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not differentiate; they prescribe tawarruk for men in the final sitting but say women sit like men. The Hanafi specification is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
This difference leads to practical variations in women's prayer.
5
Understand the underlying rationale
The Hanafi ruling is based on the principle of modesty (sitr) and ease for women, as sitting in a compact manner is more concealing and comfortable.
Istihsan (juristic preference) may override the general applicability of the hadith for women.

(474) He sits in tawarruk and recites the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) and points with the index finger in the testimony, raising it at negation and lowering it at affirmation, and does not add to the tashahhud in the first sitting, which is: 'al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu...' (Bayan al-Fiqh). (Bayan al-Fiqh, Hadith from Bayhaqi). In this hadith, during tashahhud he places the toes of the right foot towards the qiblah. Translation: (473) And the woman sits on her buttocks. Explanation: The woman sits in tawarruk in tashahhud, i.e., she places both feet to the right side and sits on her buttocks. (1) From Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi... until when it was the prostration after which the taslim is given, he put forward his left leg and sat in tawarruk on his left side (Abu Dawood, Muslim). This hadith proves that tawarruk in the final sitting is sunnah; the Hanafis specified it for women. (2) Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi said: When he sat in the final rak'ah, he put forward his left leg and erected the other and sat on his buttocks (Bukhari). (3) Athar: I said to 'Ata': Does a woman sit in the way of sitting on her left side? He said: Yes. I said: Is that dearer to you than the right? He said: Yes. He said: She sits gathered as much as she can. I said: Does she sit like the sitting of a man in the way of sitting or does she take out her left leg from under her thigh? He said: It does not harm her whichever she does if she sits gathered (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bayhaqi). In this athar, the woman sits on the left side because it is easier and more comfortable for her.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on how women should sit during tashahhud in prayer. The author first presents a hadith from Bayhaqi describing the general manner of sitting, then specifies that a woman sits on her buttocks (tawarruk). The commentary explains that the woman places both feet to the right and sits on her buttocks. Three proofs are provided: (1) A hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi in Abu Dawood and Muslim about tawarruk in the final sitting, which the Hanafi school applies specifically to women. (2) Another version of the hadith in Bukhari describing the final sitting with putting forward the left leg and erecting the right. (3) An athar from 'Ata' stating that a woman sits on her left side, and that the easiest way is acceptable. The Hanafi position is that tawarruk (sitting on the left buttock) is sunnah for women in all sittings where tashahhud is recited, based on these evidences. This ruling is part of the chapter on the composition of prayer.

Key Terms
تورك (tawarruk): Sitting on the left buttock with left leg out from under the thigh and right foot erect, or for women both feet to the right.
تشهد (tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith in the sitting of prayer.

The Preferred Tashahhud: Ibn Mas'ud's Wording
Ruling with proof: establishing the mandatory tashahhud wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the tashahhud wording, explain the evidence from the hadith, and apply the ruling to a prayer scenario.

Core Idea
The tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud is wajib because the Prophet commanded it with an imperative.

In the Hanafi school, the exact wording of the tashahhud matters. While other schools allow multiple variants, the Hanafis insist on the wording taught to Ibn Mas'ud (ra). This lesson unpacks the two key proofs from the Sunnah that establish this as the obligatory formulation in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its object
What is the legal ruling (hukm) being stated? What act does it govern? The author says the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud is 'better' (afdal) in the Hanafi school – but this 'better' is understood as wajib given the proof.
The Arabic term 'afdal' here is relative; the later evidence shows it is a binding obligation.
2
Locate the first proof and its imperative
The first proof is the hadith: 'When one of you prays, let him say (falyqul): al-tahiyyatu lillah…' Identify the imperative form 'falyqul' and understand how it indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr lil-wujub unless a qarina diverts it to recommendation.
3
Analyze the second proof: teaching like the Qur'an
The second proof states that the Prophet taught Ibn Mas'ud the tashahhud 'as he taught a surah of the Qur'an'. This shows its elevated rank. How does this strengthen the case for obligation?
While this does not directly command, it implies the tashahhud is not optional; it is a fixed part of the prayer.
4
Note the additional ruling in the first sitting
The passage adds that in the first sitting (qa'dah ula) one should not add anything beyond the tashahhud. This is a condition that follows from the obligation – any extra wording would be an innovation or at least detracting from the sunnah.
This is a practical application: the first tashahhud is shorter (only al-tahiyyatu...); the second tashahhud includes the salawat.
5
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school elevates this tashahhud to wajib, while other schools treat it as sunnah. The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, omitting it requires sajdah sahw; in other schools, it does not.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the practical difference in rulings.

Translation: (474) And he recites the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). And he points with the index finger in this manner: raising it at negation and lowering it at affirmation. And in the first sitting he does not add to the tashahhud. That tashahhud is: 'al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibatu, al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, al-salamu 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillahi al-salihin, ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluhu.' Explanation: There are several types of tashahhud; among them, reciting the tashahhud of 'Abdullah Ibn Mas'ud is considered better in the Hanafi school. Evidence: (1) 'Abdullah Ibn Mas'ud said: When we prayed behind the Prophet (peace be upon him) we used to say 'al-salamu 'ala Jibril wa Mika'il, al-salamu 'ala fulaan wa fulaan', so the Messenger of Allah turned to us and taught us: 'Indeed Allah is al-Salam, so when one of you prays, let him say: al-tahiyyatu lillahi...' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawood). In this hadith, 'faliqul' (let him say) is a command form indicating obligation, therefore the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud is better in our school. (2) In Muslim's hadith: I heard Ibn Mas'ud say: The Messenger of Allah taught me the tashahhud with his hand between my hands just as he taught me a surah of the Qur'an, and he recited the tashahhud as they recited. This hadith gives it even more importance, because the Prophet taught it like the Qur'an, and Ibn Mas'ud's hand was in the Prophet's hand, which adds to its significance. Therefore, in our school this tashahhud is better.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that the preferred tashahhud in the Hanafi school is that of 'Abdullah Ibn Mas'ud. The author gives two main proofs: First, the hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawood where the Prophet taught the Companions to say 'al-tahiyyatu lillahi...' after they had been using a different phrasing. The imperative 'falyqul' indicates obligation (wujub), making this tashahhud required. Second, the hadith where Ibn Mas'ud says the Prophet taught him the tashahhud as he taught a Surah from the Qur'an, emphasizing its importance. The text also notes that in the first sitting (qa'dah ula), one should not add anything beyond the tashahhud. The Hanafi school considers this tashahhud as the sunnah wording, and it is to be recited in all sittings of prayer where tashahhud is prescribed.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The specific wording recited in the sitting of prayer, witnessing the oneness of Allah and the prophethood of Muhammad.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation; a ruling level between fard and sunnah in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because it contains the name of the Prophet.
D) Because it was transmitted by multiple chains.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates reciting the specific tashahhud wording taught to Ibn Mas'ud (ra) because the Prophet's command 'falyqul' establishes it as wajib.

Pointing the Index Finger in Tashahhud
Method of pointing the index finger during tashahhud in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of pointing the index finger during tashahhud and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Point the index finger once without moving it—this sunnah is confirmed by multiple hadith.

The act of pointing the index finger during tashahhud is an established sunnah of the Prophet (saw). In this passage, the author presents four hadith that detail the manner of pointing. The Hanafi school derives that one should point only once, without repeated movement, and that the finger is raised at the negation and lowered at the affirmation of the shahada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being described? (Pointing the index finger during tashahhud) and what is its hukm? (Sunnah muakkadah, not wajib).
The author presents this under 'Evidence', indicating proof for a sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
Which hadith are cited? (From Wa'il ibn Hujr, 'Asim ibn Kulayb, 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn 'Umar). Identify the sources (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Bayhaqi).
All are from ahad hadith, but collectively strong.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each hadith prove the manner of pointing? The first two show making a circle and pointing; the third shows not moving the finger; the fourth shows pointing towards the qiblah with gaze fixed.
The Hanafi interpretation combines them: point once without movement.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there a difference with other schools? Yes, some schools move the finger. The Hanafi position is that moving it repeatedly is makruh.
The passage does not elaborate on ikhtilaf, but the mufta bihi is clear.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi
The operative ruling: Point once (raise at negation, lower at affirmation) without moving the finger repeatedly.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

وجه : (۱) اور شہادت کی انگلی سے اشارہ کرے اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن وائل بن حجر قال ... ثم جلس فافترش رجله اليسرى ووضع يده اليسرى على فخذه اليسرى وحد مرفقه الايمن على فخذه اليمنى وقبض ثنتين و حلق حلقة ورأيته يقول هكذا وحلق بشر الابهام والوسطى واشار بالسبابة (ابوداؤد شریف، باب كيف الجلوس في التشهد ، ص ۱۴۶، نمبر ۹۵۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ انگوٹھے اور درمیان کی انگلی سے حلقہ بنائے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے اشارہ کرے(۳) عاصم بن كليب الجرمي عن ابيه عن جده قال دخلت على النبي علة وهو يصلى وقد وضع يده اليسرى عـلـى فـخـذه اليسرى ووضع يده اليمنى على فخذه اليمنى وقبض اصابعه وبسط السبابة ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ابواب الدعاء ج ثانی ، ص ۸۱۷، نمبر ۳۵۸۷ رنسائی شریف ، باب قبض المثنتين من اصابع اليد اليمنى وعقد الوسطی ، ص ۱۷۶، نمبر ۱۲۶۹) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ حلقہ بنائے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے اشارہ کرے ۔ (۴) صرف ایک مرتبہ اشارہ کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله انه ذكر ان النبي الا الله كان يشير باصبعه اذا دعا لا یحرکھا ۔ (سنن بیہقی، باب من روی انہ انشار بھا ولم سحر کھا ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۸۹، نمبر ۲۷۸۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بار بار حرکت نہیں کرتے تھے صرف ایک بار اشارہ کرتے تھے۔ عن ابن عمر انه رای رجلا يحرك الحصا..... قال فوضع يده الـيـمـنـى عـلـى فـخـذه و اشار باصبعه التي تلى الابهام في القبلة و رمى ببصره اليها او نحوها ثم قال هكذا
Evidence: (1) And he points with the index finger. For this, the hadith is: from Wa'il ibn Hujr... Then he sat, spread his left leg, placed his left hand on his left thigh, placed his right elbow on his right thigh, grasped two fingers and made a circle, and I saw him saying like this, making a circle with his thumb and middle finger, and pointing with the index finger (Abu Dawood). This hadith indicates making a circle with thumb and middle finger and pointing with the index finger. (3) 'Asim ibn Kulayb al-Jarmi from his father from his grandfather said: I entered upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) while he was praying, and he had placed his left hand on his left thigh and his right hand on his right thigh, he grasped his fingers and extended the index finger (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i). This hadith also says to make a circle and point with the index finger. (4) He points only once. For this, the hadith is: from 'Abdullah that he mentioned that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to point with his finger when supplicating and did not move it (Bayhaqi). This hadith indicates that he did not move it repeatedly, but rather pointed only once. From Ibn 'Umar that he saw a man moving pebbles... He placed his right hand on his thigh and pointed with the finger next to the thumb towards the qiblah, and cast his glance towards it or towards something, then said: This is what I saw the Messenger of Allah doing.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage details the method of pointing the index finger during tashahhud in the Hanafi school. The author presents several hadith proofs. First, the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr describes the Prophet making a circle with thumb and middle finger and pointing with the index finger. Second, the hadith of 'Asim ibn Kulayb confirms making a circle and extending the index finger. Third, a hadith from 'Abdullah states that the Prophet pointed only once without moving it repeatedly. Fourth, a narration from Ibn 'Umar shows the Prophet placing his right hand on his thigh, pointing with the finger next to the thumb towards the qiblah, and fixing his gaze on it. The Hanafi school derives that one should point the index finger once, raising it at the negation 'La ilaha' and lowering it at the affirmation 'illa Allah', based on the phrase 'رفعها عند النفي ويضعها عند الاثبات' mentioned earlier in the text (though not repeated here). The act is considered a sunnah of the prayer.

Key Terms
مسبحة (mushabbiha (or sababa)): The index finger used for pointing during tashahhud.
اشارة (ishara): The act of pointing the index finger during the testimony of faith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how should one point the index finger during tashahhud?
A) One should move it continuously throughout the tashahhud.
B) One should point only once, without moving it.
C) One should point with the right hand and move it in a circular motion.
D) One should not point at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that pointing the index finger once without repeated movement during tashahhud is a confirmed sunnah.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Tashahhud: Wajib Not Fard
This passage establishes the wording and obligation level of tashahhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the tashahhud and explain why it is classified as wajib rather than fard.

Core Idea
The tashahhud is wajib, not fard, because the command is from an ahad hadith.

The tashahhud is a key component of prayer. This lesson examines the specific wording transmitted by Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and the evidence for its level of obligation in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled? The recitation of tashahhud. What is the hukm? Wajib, as stated by the author.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud with the imperative 'faliyaqul'.
The hadith is in Muslim, Abu Dawud, etc.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the imperative indicate obligation? In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub. But because the hadith is ahad, the obligation is wajib, not fard.
Thubut: zanni; dalala: zanni.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers tashahhud as fard, possibly relying on the same or different hadith.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the Ibn Mas'ud wording and the classification of the hadith as ahad.
Mufta bihi: the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud.
