The Obligation of Recitation and Its Necessity for the Imam
Proving the condition of recitation for imamate with two textual proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and hadith evidence that recitation in prayer is fard and explain why an imam must be able to recite correctly.

Core Idea
The imam must be able to recite because recitation is fard and prayer without it is invalid.

This lesson examines the condition of recitation (qira'ah) for the imam. Using a Quranic verse and a prophetic hadith, the text establishes that recitation is an obligatory act in prayer. Therefore, a person who cannot recite cannot lead the prayer, as his deficiency would invalidate the prayer for himself and his followers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic proof
The verse 'So recite what is easy from it' (73:20) uses an imperative, which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (wujub). This establishes that recitation is a fard act in prayer.
The imperative 'faqra'ū' is the key linguistic indicator.
2
Identify the hadith proof
The hadith 'There is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a sūrah' explicitly negates the validity of prayer without recitation, making it a condition.
This hadith is from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud; though ahad, it is accepted in this context.
3
Connect to imamate
Since recitation is a fard pillar, the imam must be able to perform it. If he cannot recite, his own prayer is invalid, and he cannot lead others in a valid prayer.
The imam's inability renders his imamate invalid for that prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۸۰)[۵] قرات۔ تشریح : نماز میں قرآت فرض ہے اور امام کو قرآت ہی نہیں آتی تو امامت کیسے کرے گا ! وجه : (۱) فاقرء وا ما تيسر منه واقيموا الصلوة و آتو الزكوة ( آیت ۲۰ ، سورة المزمل ۷۳ ) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں قرآت پڑھنا فرض ہے، اور جسکو قرآت نہیں آتی وہ اس فرض کی آدائگی سے محروم ہے اس لئے وہ امامت کے قابل نہیں ہے (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ قرآت کے بغیر نماز نہیں ہوگی۔ عن ابی سعید قال قال رسول الله مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم ولا صلوة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد وسورة في فريضة او غيرها. ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی تحریم الصلوة و تحلیلها، ص۶۶ نمبر ۲۳۸ ابوداؤد شریف، باب الامام يحدث بعد ما يرفع رأسه من آخر رکعتہ ص ۱۰۰ نمبر (۶۱۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قرآت کئے بغیر نماز نہیں ہوگی۔
Translation: (480) [5] Recitation. Explanation: Recitation in prayer is fard, and if the imam does not know recitation, how can he lead? Proof: (1) 'So recite what is easy from it and establish prayer and give zakah' (Surah al-Muzzammil 73:20). From this verse it is known that recitation in prayer is fard, and the one who cannot recite is deprived of performing this fard, so he is not fit for imamate. (2) In this hadith also: 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrīm is takbīr, its tahlīl is taslīm, and there is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a sūrah in an obligatory or other prayer.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) This hadith states that there is no prayer without recitation.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage proves the necessity of recitation for the imam by citing two proofs. First, the Quranic verse from Surah al-Muzzammil (73:20) commands recitation in prayer, making it a fard (obligatory act). Since the imam's role includes fulfilling this fard for himself and the followers, he must be able to recite correctly. Second, the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri explicitly states that prayer is invalid without reciting Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah, whether the prayer is obligatory or supererogatory. Thus, a person who cannot recite cannot serve as imam, as his inability would lead to the invalidity of the prayer.

Key Terms
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of the Quran in prayer, which is a fard act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Surah al-Muzzammil 73:20
C) Surah al-Baqarah 2:238
D) Surah al-Ikhlas 112:1

Key Takeaway
Recitation is obligatory (fard) in prayer; therefore an imam must be able to recite correctly, or his imamate is invalid.

Ruling on Excused Imam: Nosebleed and Speech Defects
Defining excuses that prevent valid imamate and providing supporting proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the excuses that invalidate imamate in the Hanafi school and state the ruling for each.

Core Idea
An excused imam with defective recitation invalidates followers' prayer because his recitation substitutes for theirs.

The Hanafi school sets strict conditions for the imam's recitation. This lesson explains the excuses that prevent valid imamate – continuous nosebleed and speech defects – and the proof from hadith that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The text states: a person with an excuse cannot lead those without the excuse. Recognize that this principle governs all specific cases.
2
List the specific excuses
Extract the four excuses mentioned: continuous nosebleed (ru'af), fa'fa'ah (repeating 'fa'), tamtamah (repeating 'ta'/'ma'), and lathgh (substituting letters like 'ra' for 'ghayn').
These defects prevent correct Qur'anic recitation.
3
Understand why these excuses invalidate
Each excuse causes the imam's recitation to be incorrect. Since the imam's recitation stands for the follower's, the follower's prayer becomes invalid if the imam's recitation is defective.
The hadith 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is a recitation for him' is the key proof.
4
Determine the ruling
Conclude that the imamate is invalid (fasid); such an imam cannot lead, and if he does, the followers must repeat their prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۸۱) [۲] عذروں سے سلامت ہونا، جیسے نکسیر اور جس کے کلام میں پہلے فافا‘ نکلے ، اور جس کے کلام میں 'ت “ اور ”م‘ نکلے، اور جس کی زبان کی جانب اور “ سے ”غ‘ کی طرف متحرک ہو جائے۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں جو آدمی معذور ہو وہ غیر معذور کی امامت نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے جس کو مسلسل نکسیر ہے وہ غیر نکسیر والے کی امامت نہیں کراسکتا۔ اسی طرح جن کی قرآت میں رف نکلتا ہو، یا رت نکلتا ہو، یا رغ ، نکلتا ہو تو اس کی قرآت درست نہیں ہے، امام کی قرآت مقتدی کی قرآت ہوتی ہے، اور جب امام کی قرآت نہیں ہوئی تو مقتدی کی بھی قرآت نہیں ہوئی اس لئے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، اس لئے یہ امامت نہیں کر سکتا۔ وجه : (۱) عن جابر قال قال رسول الله الله من كان له امام فقراء ة الامام له قراء ة . ( ابن ماجہ شریف، باب اذا قرء الامام فانصتوا ص ۱۲۰، نمبر ۸۵۰ر دارقطنی ، باب ذکر قوله من کان له امام ، ص ۱۳۲۱ نمبر ۱۲۲۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام کی قرآت مقتدی کے لئے کافی اور زبان میں کمزوری کی وجہ سے امام نے قرآت نہیں کی تو مقتدی نے بھی قرآت نہیں کی اس لئے اس کی امامت درست نہیں (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله لا لا لا له الامام ضامن والمؤذن مؤتمن (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء ان الامام ضامن والمؤذن مؤتمن ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۲۰۷ رابن ماجبته ، باب ما ستجب على الامام ، ص ۱۳۸، نمبر (۹۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام ضامن ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو قرآت اچھی آنی چاہئے ، یا معذور نہیں ہونا چاہئے ۔ لغت : الرعاف: ناک سے مسلسل خون بہنا، نکسیر پھوٹنا۔ الفافة: جس کی زبان سے ہر لفظ میں ف، نکلے، ہونٹ کی بندش کمزور ہونے سے ہر لفظ میں ف، نکلتا ہے۔ اہتمتمہ : جس کی زبان سے ہر لفظ میں بت، ہم نکل جائے ، زبان پر بندش کمزور ہونے سے ایسا ہوتا ہے۔ اللغ : زبان ہیں، نکالنا چاہے تو ہٹ نکل جائے ، پر نکالنا چا ہے تو غ نکل جائے۔ ان صورتوں میں قرآت صحیح نہیں ہوتی۔
Translation: (481) [2] Freedom from excuses, such as nosebleed and one in whose speech 'fa' appears first, and one in whose speech 'ta' and 'ma' appear, and one whose tongue moves from one letter to another like from 'ra' to 'ghayn'. Explanation: These issues are based on the principle that a person who has an excuse cannot lead those who are not excused. Therefore, the one who has continuous nosebleed cannot lead those without nosebleed. Similarly, those in whose recitation 'ra' appears, or 'ta' appears, or 'ghayn' appears, their recitation is not correct. The imam's recitation is the follower's recitation, and when the imam's recitation is invalid, the follower's recitation is also invalid, so the prayer becomes invalid. Therefore, such a person cannot lead. Proof: (1) From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is a recitation for him.' (Ibn Majah, Daruqutni) This hadith states that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower, and due to weakness in the tongue, the imam did not recite, so the follower also did not recite, so his imamate is not valid. (2) From Abu Hurairah, he said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Indeed, the imam is a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin is a trustee.' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) From this hadith, it is known that the imam is a guarantor. Therefore, he should have good recitation or not be excused. Vocabulary: Ar-ru'af: continuous bleeding from the nose, nosebleed. Al-fa'fa'ah: one from whose tongue 'fa' comes out in every word, due to weak lip closure, 'fa' comes out in every word. At-tamtamah: one from whose tongue 'ta' and 'ha' and 'ma' come out, due to weak tongue closure. Al-lugh: the tongue; when he wants to say 'ra', 'ghayn' comes out, and when he wants to say 'ghayn', 'ra' comes out. In these cases, recitation is not correct.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage defines the excuses that prevent valid imamate and provides proofs. The author first states the general principle: an excused person cannot lead non-excused. Then he specifies examples: continuous nosebleed (ru'af), stammering (fa'fa'ah), stuttering (tamtamah), and lisp (lathgh). The reason is that these defects prevent correct recitation. Since the imam's recitation stands for the follower's recitation (based on the hadith 'the imam's recitation is a recitation for him'), any defect in the imam's recitation invalidates the follower's prayer. Two hadiths are cited: one establishes that the imam's recitation suffices, and the other states that the imam is a guarantor (ضامن), meaning he is responsible for the prayer's validity. The lexical definitions clarify each defect. The overall ruling: an imam with any of these defects cannot lead those without the same defect.

Key Terms
الرعاف (al-ru'af): Continuous bleeding from the nose (nosebleed) that prevents proper recitation.
الفأفأة (al-fa'fa'ah): A speech defect where the speaker repeatedly utters 'fa' due to weak lips.
التمتمة (al-tamtamah): A speech defect where the speaker repeats 'ta' or 'ma' due to tongue weakness.
اللثغ (al-lathgh): A lisp where the speaker substitutes one letter for another, e.g., 'ra' for 'ghayn'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An imam with a continuous nosebleed or a speech defect that makes his recitation incorrect cannot lead those without the defect; his imamate is invalid and followers must repeat the prayer.

Loss of a Condition for Imamate
Stating that if a condition of prayer is missing, imamate is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of prayer that an imam must fulfill, and explain why the absence of any condition invalidates his imamate.

Core Idea
An imam's prayer must be valid for his imamate to be valid; missing a condition invalidates both.

This lesson focuses on a fundamental rule: the imam must satisfy all conditions of prayer before leading others. The text specifically mentions purification from both minor and major impurities, and covering the private parts. If the imam's own prayer is invalid due to a missing condition, the followers' prayer cannot be valid either. This ruling is a cornerstone for understanding the validity of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
First, recognize that the passage states a clear ruling: imamate is invalid when a condition of prayer is missing.
The ruling is unconditional; it applies regardless of the followers' awareness.
2
List the conditions mentioned
The text explicitly names two conditions: purification (taharah) and covering the private parts (satr al-awrah). Understand that these are prerequisites for prayer itself.
In Hanafi fiqh, conditions must be present before starting prayer.
3
Understand the logical connection
The rationale given is that if the imam's prayer is invalid due to a missing condition, then the follower's prayer, which depends on the imam, is also invalid. This is based on the principle that the imam's state must be valid for the congregation's prayer to be valid.
This logic applies to all conditions of prayer, not just the two mentioned.
4
Apply the ruling
Consider a scenario: an imam leads prayer without wudu. His prayer is invalid, so the followers' prayer is also invalid. They must repeat the prayer.
The same applies if the imam's awrah is exposed, even unintentionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۸۲) وفقد شرط كطهارة وستر عورة. تشریح : نماز کی جو شرائط ہیں مثلا امام حدث اصغر اور حدث اکبر سے پاک ہو، یا ستر عورت ہو، وہ شرطیں پائی جائیں تب امامت درست ہوگی ، اور اگر وہ نہ ہوں تو امامت درست نہیں ہوگی، کیونکہ ان شرطوں کے مفقود ہونے سے خود امام کی نماز نہیں ہوگی تو مقتدی کی نماز کیسے ہو جائے گی۔
Translation: (482) And the loss of a condition such as purification and covering of the private parts. Explanation: The conditions of prayer, for example, the imam being free from minor and major ritual impurity, or covering the private parts—if these conditions are found, then imamate is valid; and if they are not, then imamate is not valid, because with the loss of these conditions, the imam's own prayer is not valid, so how can the follower's prayer be valid?
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward ruling: the imam must fulfill all the conditions of prayer for his imamate to be valid. The conditions mentioned are purification from both minor and major impurities (hadath asghar and akbar) and covering the private parts (satr al-awrah). The logic is simple: if the imam's own prayer is invalid due to missing a condition, then the followers' prayer, which depends on him, will also be invalid. This is a general principle that reinforces that the imam's state must be perfect for the prayer to be correct.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition; here, a prerequisite for the validity of prayer, such as purification and covering the private parts.
طهارة (taharah): Ritual purity, both from minor hadath (wudu) and major hadath (ghusl).
ستر عورة (satr al-awrah): Covering the private parts (for men, from navel to knees; for women, the whole body except face, hands, and feet).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The followers' prayer is valid if they did not know.

Key Takeaway
An imam must fulfill all conditions of prayer; if any condition is missing, his imamate and the followers' prayer are invalid.

Defective Imam Cannot Lead Prayer
Ruling that a person with a chronic defect cannot lead prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an imam with a chronic defect and apply the hadith 'qira'atu al-imami lahu qira'ah' to explain why his imamate is invalid.

Core Idea
An imam with a chronic defect invalidates his recitation and thus the follower's prayer.

This passage from the Chapter of Imamate establishes a fundamental principle: a person who is ma'dhur (excused) due to a chronic condition cannot lead someone who is not ma'dhur. The text gives concrete examples—continuous nosebleed (ru'af) and speech impediments (alfa, itatmama, lagh)—and cites two hadith to prove that the imam's recitation must be correct for the follower's prayer to be valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leading prayer by a person with a chronic defect. The ruling: such imamate is invalid.
The defect must be chronic and affect recitation or purity.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: (1) 'The recitation of the imam is recitation for the follower' (Ibn Majah, al-Daraqutni). (2) 'The imam is a guarantor' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah).
Both are ahad hadith, providing zanni proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith shows that the imam's recitation substitutes for the follower's; if the imam's recitation is defective, the follower's recitation is also defective, invalidating the prayer. The second hadith emphasizes the imam's responsibility, so he must be free from defects.
Hanafi usul: al-amr bi al-imam al-sahih yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not require the imam's recitation to be free from minor defects as long as it is understandable.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in the application of the hadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the apparent meaning of the hadith and the principle that the imam is a guarantor. The mufta bihi is that such a person cannot lead.
Tarjih based on stronger dalala according to Hanafi usul.

Chapter of Imamate. (482) And the loss of a condition, like purity and covering of the private parts. Explanation: These issues are based on the principle that a person who is excused cannot lead one who is not excused. Therefore, one who has a continuous nosebleed cannot lead one who does not have a nosebleed. Similarly, if in recitation the letter 'ra' comes out as 'ghayn', or 'ya' as 'ta', or 'ghayn' as something else, his recitation is not correct. The recitation of the imam is the recitation of the follower, and when the imam's recitation is not correct, the follower's recitation is also not correct, so the prayer becomes invalid. Therefore, such a person cannot lead. Proof: (1) From Jabir, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is recitation for him.' (Ibn Majah, chapter: When the imam recites, be silent, p. 120, no. 850; al-Daraqutni, chapter: Mention of the saying 'Whoever has an imam', p. 1321, no. 1220). This hadith indicates that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower, and due to weakness in speech, the imam did not recite correctly, so the follower also did not recite, therefore his imamate is not valid. (2) From Abu Huraira, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The imam is a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin is entrusted.' (Tirmidhi, chapter: What has come about the imam being a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin being entrusted, p. 158, no. 207; Ibn Majah, chapter: What is obligatory upon the imam, p. 138, no. (98)). From this hadith it is known that the imam is a guarantor. Therefore, he should have good recitation or should not be excused. Lexicon: al-ru'af: continuous bleeding from the nose; al-alfa: one from whose tongue the letter 'fa' comes out in every word due to weakness of lip closure; al-itatmama: one from whose tongue the letter 'ta' or 'tha' comes out due to weakness of tongue; al-lagh: one who when he intends to pronounce a letter, another letter comes out. In these cases, recitation is not correct. Translation: (482) The condition of prayer should not be missing, such as purity and covering of the private parts. Explanation: The conditions of prayer, such as the imam being free from minor and major impurity, or covering the private parts, should be present for imamate to be valid. If they are not present, imamate is not valid, because if these conditions are missing, the imam's own prayer is not valid, so how can the follower's prayer be valid?
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on imamate. It establishes a key principle: a person who is excused (ma'dhur) due to a chronic condition cannot lead someone who is not excused. The text gives examples: continuous nosebleed (ru'af) and speech impediments (alfat, itatmama, lagh) that prevent correct recitation. Since the imam's recitation suffices for the follower (as per the hadith 'the imam's recitation is recitation for the follower'), any defect in the imam's recitation invalidates the follower's recitation as well, thus invalidating the prayer. The second hadith establishes the imam as a guarantor (damin), meaning he is responsible for the prayer's validity, so he must be free from defects. The commentary elaborates that the fundamental conditions of prayer (purity, covering the private parts) must be present in the imam for his imamate to be valid.

Key Terms
الرعاف (al-ru'af): Continuous nosebleed
الفافة (al-alfa): A speech defect where the letter 'fa' comes out due to lip weakness
اہتمتمہ (al-itatmama): A speech defect where 'ta' or 'tha' comes out due to tongue weakness
اللغ (al-lagh): A speech defect where intended letters are substituted unintentionally

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the imam must be in state of purity at all times.

Key Takeaway
An imam with a chronic defect that affects his recitation or purity cannot lead prayer, as his defective recitation invalidates the follower's prayer.

The First Condition of Iqtida: Intention at the Takbir
Listing fourteen conditions, focusing on the first: intention to follow at the takbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for valid following (iqtida) and explain its necessity using the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.

Core Idea
Following the imam requires deliberate intention at the takbir — without it, the congregation is invalid.

The Hanafi school strictly requires the follower to have the intention of following the imam at the time of his own opening takbir. This condition distinguishes congregational prayer from individual prayer and is rooted in the hadith 'The imam is appointed only to be followed.' In this lesson, we examine this condition, its proof, and the scholarly discussion around it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
From the passage, extract the first condition for valid iqtida. Note the exact wording: 'The follower intends to follow the imam at the time of his takbir.'
This condition is about the follower's internal state.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited by the author: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed...' from Bukhari and Muslim. Note its chain (Anas ibn Malik) and its status as a hadith ahad.
The hadith is zanni in both thubut and dalala.
3
Understand wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the phrase 'liyu'tama bihi' (to be followed) implies that the follower must deliberately intend to follow. Mere physical coordination does not fulfill the meaning of 'following'.
This is the key linguistic argument in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Contrast the Hanafi position with the Maliki view that intention is only recommended. The Shafi'i school agrees with Hanafi that intention is a condition.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in Hanafi, lack of intention invalidates the iqtida.
5
See the thamarah
Apply the condition: if a follower does not intend to follow at the takbir, his iqtida is invalid. He would be praying individually, not in congregation.
This affects the validity of the congregational prayer and its rewards.

Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage begins by stating that there are fourteen conditions for the validity of following (iqtida) the imam. It enumerates these conditions in list form, though some are only partially given. The focus of the explanation is the first condition: the follower must intend to follow the imam at the time of his own takbir (the opening 'Allahu Akbar'). The commentary explains that the imam is a guarantor (damin) for the prayer's validity, so the follower's intention to follow must coincide with his own initiation of prayer. This is supported by the well-known hadith: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed...', which establishes the principle that the follower's actions follow the imam's. The intention (niyyah) is essential because it distinguishes a congregational prayer from an individual one; without it, the follower is praying alone, which defeats the purpose of congregation.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship
تحريمه (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer
متابعة (mutaba'ah): Following the imam in all actions of prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The follower must intend to follow the imam at the time of his own takbir.
C) The imam and follower must be in the same place.
D) The follower must know the imam's intention.

Key Takeaway
The first condition for valid iqtida is that the follower must have the specific intention to follow the imam at the moment of his own opening takbir, based on the hadith 'innama ju'ila al-imamu liyu'tama bihi'.

Four Conditions for Valid Iqtida: Intention, Imam's Lead, and Position
Listing and explaining the first four conditions for valid following of the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first four conditions for valid iqtida and explain the Hanafi proofs for each, including the intra-madhhab dispute on the imam's intention to lead women.

Core Idea
Following the imam requires intention at starting takbir, imam's lead in position and prayer degree, and intention to lead women when they follow.

This lesson unpacks the foundational rules of congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school. We will examine four key conditions that ensure the follower's prayer is validly connected to the imam's, with evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, and athar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is iqtida (following the imam). The ruling: it is valid (sahih) or invalid (fasid) based on fulfilling these conditions.
These are shurut (conditions), not arkan (pillars).
2
State the first condition and its proof
The follower must intend to follow the imam at the moment of his own takbir tahrimah. Proof: hadith 'The imam is only appointed to be followed' and Quran 2:43 'bow with those who bow'.
The hadith implies connection at the start.
3
Examine the second condition and its dispute
For women's iqtida, the imam must intend to lead them. The text discusses a second riwaya allowing it without intention if the woman stands behind. Identify the mufta bihi view and its basis.
Focus on the risk of prayer invalidation if woman stands alongside man.
4
State the third and fourth conditions
Third: imam's heel must be ahead of follower. Fourth: imam cannot be praying a lower degree prayer. Note the proofs: hadith of Anas and general principle.
These ensure the imam's precedence and the follower's full participation.

( بخاری شریف، باب صلاة القاعد، ص ۱۷۸ نمبر ۱۴ار مسلم شریف ، باب انتمام المأموم بالامام ص ۱۷۴، نمبر (۴۸۴) ونية الرجل الامامة شرط لصحة اقتداء النساء به (۴۸۵) وتقدّم الامام بعقبه عن الماموم ۴۱۱ ۹۲۱٫ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام اقتداء کے لئے ہے اس لئے اس کے تحریے کے ساتھ جڑنا ضروری ہے۔ (۲) واقیموا الصلوۃ و آتو الزکوۃ واركعوامع الراکعین ۔ ( آیت ۴۳ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ رکوع کرنے والوں کے ساتھ رکوع کرو، جس کے اشارہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مقتدی کا تحریمہ امام کے تحریمے کے ساتھ ملا ہوا ہو۔ ترجمه : (۴۸۴) [۲] اور عورتوں کی اقتداء صیح ہونے کے لئے مرد کی امامت کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے۔ تشریح : عورت امام کی اقتداء کرے یہ اس وقت درست ہوگی جبکہ امام نے باضابطہ عورت کے امام بنے کی نیت کی ہو، اور اگر عورت کے امام بنے کی نیت نہ کرے تو عورت کا اقتداء کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ لیکن دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت پیچھے کھڑی ہوتو امام اس کی نیت نہ کرے تب بھی امام کی اقتدا کرنا جائز ہے۔ وجه : (۱) حنفیہ کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ عورت اور مرد کی نیت ایک ہو اور عورت مرد کے ساتھ کھڑی ہوگئی تو مرد کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ چونکہ محاذات سے مرد کی نماز فاسد ہونے کا خطرہ ہے اس لئے عورت کی امامت کی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے (۲) اخبرنا ابو حنيفة عن حماد عن ابرهيم قال اذا صلت المرأة الى جانب الرجل وكانا في صلوة واحدة فسدت صلوته.قال محمد و به ناخذ وهو قول ابي حنيفة دوسرے اثر میں یہ ہے . انـمـا تفسد عليه اذا صلت الى جانبه و هما في صلوة واحدة ، تـأتـم بـه أو يـأتـمـان بغيرهما ، وهو قول ابي حنيفة - ( كتاب الآثار لا مام محمد ، باب ما يقطع الصلوۃ ،ص ۲۷، نمبر ۱۳۷، نمبر ۱۳۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نماز متحد ہو تو فاسد ہوگی۔ (۳) یہ حدیث اگر چہ منسوخ مانی جاتی ہے، لیکن اس سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة قال : قال رسول الله الله : يقطع الصلوة المرأة ، و الحمار ، و الكلب ، ويقى ذالك مثل موءخرة الرحل - (مسلم شریف، باب قدر مایستر المصلی ص ۲۰۹، نمبر ۱۱۳۹/۵۱۱ ابوداود شریف، باب ما لقطع الصلوۃ ص ۱۱ نمبر ۷۰۲) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ عورت کے سامنے آنے سے نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی۔ ترجمه : (۳۸۵) [۳] اور امام کی ایڑی مقتدی سے آگے ہو۔ تشریح : امام کی شان یہ ہے کہ وہ مقتدی سے تھوڑا آگے ہو اس لئے امام کی ایڑی مقتدی سے آگے ہو تو آگے سمجھا جائے گا۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث کے اشارے سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک قال صليت اناو یتیم فی بیتنا خلف النبي وامي خلفنا ام سلیم بخاری شریف، باب المرأة وحدها تكون صفا ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۷۲۷ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب اذا کانوا ثلثہ کیف لیقومون جی ۹۷ نمبر ۶۱۲) اس حدیث میں مقتدی کو پیچھے کھڑا کیا جس سے استدلال کیا جاسکتا ہے کہ ایک مقتدی ہو تب بھی وہ تھوڑا پیچھے رہے۔ ترجمه : (۴۸۶) [۴] اور امام مقتدی سے کم درجہ کی نماز پڑھنے والا نہ ہو۔
And the conditions for the validity of following are fourteen things. (483) The follower intends to follow at the time of his tahrimah (saying Allahu Akbar). ... And for the validity of women following, the man must intend to lead. And the imam's heel should be ahead of the follower. And the imam should not be praying a lower degree of prayer than the follower. Translation: (283) [1] The follower intends to follow at the time of his tahrimah. Explanation: In making prayer invalid or valid, the imam is responsible for the follower, so at the moment he ties his tahrimah, the follower must intend to follow that imam; then his iqtida will be valid. Proof: (a) From Anas ibn Malik ... he said: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed; when he says takbir, say takbir; when he bows, bow; when he raises, raise.' (Bukhari, chapter on prayer of the sitting, p. 178 no. ...; Muslim, chapter on following the imam, p. 174 no.) This hadith states that the imam is for following, so it is necessary to connect with his takbir. (2) 'And establish prayer and give zakat and bow with those who bow' (Quran 2:43). This verse indicates bowing with those who bow, which suggests that the follower's tahrimah should be connected with the imam's tahrimah. Translation: (484) [2] And for the validity of women following, the man's intention to lead is a condition. Explanation: A woman's following of the imam is valid only when the imam has explicitly intended to lead the woman; if he does not intend to lead the woman, her following is not valid. However, there is another narration that if the woman stands behind, even if the imam does not intend for her, her following is permissible. Proof: (1) The Hanafi position is that the intention of the woman and man is one, and if the woman stands alongside the man, the man's prayer becomes invalid. Since there is a risk of his prayer being invalidated due to being in line with her, it is necessary to intend to lead the woman. (2) Abu Hanifa narrated from Hammad from Ibrahim: He said, 'When a woman prays beside a man, and both are in one prayer, his prayer becomes invalid.' Muhammad said: 'We adopt this, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa.' In another athar: 'It only becomes invalid for him when she prays beside him and both are in one prayer, whether she follows him or they both follow someone else, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa.' (Kitab al-Athar of Imam Muhammad, chapter on what cuts the prayer, p. 27, nos. 137, 138). This athar states that if the prayer is united, it becomes invalid. (3) Although this hadith is considered abrogated, it supports it: From Abu Hurairah, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The woman, the donkey, and the dog cut the prayer, and that is like the back of a saddle.' (Muslim, chapter on what covers the one praying, p. 209, no. 1139/511; Abu Dawud, chapter on what cuts the prayer, p. 11, no. 702). This hadith indicates that the appearance of a woman cuts the prayer. Translation: (385) [3] And the imam's heel should be ahead of the follower. Explanation: The dignity of the imam is that he should be slightly ahead of the follower; therefore, if the imam's heel is ahead of the follower, he is considered ahead. Proof: (1) This can be inferred from the indication of this hadith: From Anas ibn Malik, he said: 'I prayed with an orphan in our house behind the Prophet, and my mother Umm Sulaim was behind us.' (Bukhari, chapter on the woman alone forming a row, p. 188, no. 727; Abu Dawud, chapter on when they are three how they should stand, p. 97, no. 612). In this hadith, the follower is placed behind, from which it can be inferred that even if there is one follower, he should be slightly behind. Translation: (486) [4] And the imam should not be praying a lower degree of prayer than the follower.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the first four of fourteen conditions for the validity of iqtida (following the imam in congregational prayer) according to the Hanafi school. The author explains each condition with its proofs from hadith and Quran. The first condition requires the follower to intend to follow the imam at the moment of his own takbir tahrimah (opening takbir). This is based on the hadith 'The imam is only appointed to be followed' and the Quranic verse 'bow with those who bow', indicating that the follower's prayer must be connected to the imam's. The second condition concerns women following a male imam: the imam must intend to lead women. The text notes a difference within the Hanafi school: one view requires the intention, another (weaker) view allows it without intention if the woman stands behind. The proofs include the risk of prayer invalidation if a woman stands alongside a man, based on athar from Ibrahim and Abu Hanifa. The third condition states that the imam should be slightly ahead of the follower, with his heel ahead. This is derived from the hadith where the Prophet placed followers behind him. The fourth condition is that the imam cannot be praying a prayer of a lower degree (e.g., a nafl imam leading a fard follower) – this is stated but not elaborated here. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each condition and its proof.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer, where the follower intends to perform the prayer behind the imam and follows his actions.
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer, after which certain actions become prohibited (haram).
متابعت (mutaba'ah): Following the imam in actions; the follower must intend to follow the imam at the moment of his own tahrimah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the validity of iqtida according to the first condition explained?
A) The follower must be older than the imam
B) The follower must intend to follow the imam at the time of his own takbir tahrimah
C) The imam must be ahead of the follower by at least one meter
D) The follower must be a male

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets four foundational conditions for valid iqtida: intention to follow at the start, imam's intention to lead women when present, imam's physical precedence, and the imam not praying a lesser degree prayer.

Imam's Intention Required for Women's Following
States ruling and proofs on imam's intention for women followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's intention for women followers and apply it to a congregation scenario.

Core Idea
A woman's prayer behind a male imam is invalid unless he intends to lead her.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: the imam must consciously intend to lead any women in the congregation. This requirement stems from the risk of muhadhat (alignment) invalidating the man's prayer. We will explore the proofs and the intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The ruling states that the imam's intention to lead women is a condition for the validity of their following. Without it, the women's prayer is invalid.
This is the mufta bihi (operative position).
2
Understand the risk of muhadhat
The underlying reason is that if a woman prays beside a man in the same congregation, his prayer becomes invalid. This concern drives the requirement.
Muhadhat (alignment) is a key concept in Hanafi fiqh for prayer invalidation.
3
Examine the primary proof
The athar from Ibrahim reported by Abu Hanifa states: 'If a woman prays next to a man and they are in one prayer, his prayer becomes invalid.' This is the direct evidence.
Imam Muhammad explicitly says: 'We adopt this, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa.'
4
Note the intra-madhhab difference
A second narration exists: if the woman stands behind the imam, the intention is not required, and her following is valid.
This narration is not relied upon in fatwa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Imam Muhammad's adoption of Abu Hanifa's view gives it greater weight. Thus, the requirement of intention is the relied-upon position.
The fatwa is on the first view.

Source Text

(۴۸۴) ونية الرجل الامامة شرط لصحة اقتداء النساء به

ترجمه : (۴۸۴) [۲] اور عورتوں کی اقتداء صیح ہونے کے لئے مرد کی امامت کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے۔ تشریح : عورت امام کی اقتداء کرے یہ اس وقت درست ہوگی جبکہ امام نے باضابطہ عورت کے امام بنے کی نیت کی ہو، اور اگر عورت کے امام بنے کی نیت نہ کرے تو عورت کا اقتداء کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ لیکن دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت پیچھے کھڑی ہوتو امام اس کی نیت نہ کرے تب بھی امام کی اقتدا کرنا جائز ہے۔
وجه : (۱) حنفیہ کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ عورت اور مرد کی نیت ایک ہو اور عورت مرد کے ساتھ کھڑی ہوگئی تو مرد کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ چونکہ محاذات سے مرد کی نماز فاسد ہونے کا خطرہ ہے اس لئے عورت کی امامت کی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے (۲) اخبرنا ابو حنيفة عن حماد عن ابرهيم قال اذا صلت المرأة الى جانب الرجل وكانا في صلوة واحدة فسدت صلوته.قال محمد و به ناخذ وهو قول ابي حنيفة دوسرے اثر میں یہ ہے . انـمـا تفسد عليه اذا صلت الى جانبه و هما في صلوة واحدة ، تـأتـم بـه أو يـأتـمـان بغيرهما ، وهو قول ابي حنيفة - ( كتاب الآثار لا مام محمد ، باب ما يقطع الصلوۃ ،ص ۲۷، نمبر ۱۳۷، نمبر ۱۳۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نماز متحد ہو تو فاسد ہوگی۔ (۳) یہ حدیث اگر چہ منسوخ مانی جاتی ہے، لیکن اس سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة قال : قال رسول الله الله : يقطع الصلوة المرأة ، و الحمار ، و الكلب ، ويقى ذالك مثل موءخرة الرحل - (مسلم شریف، باب قدر مایستر المصلی ص ۲۰۹، نمبر ۱۱۳۹/۵۱۱ ابوداود شریف، باب ما لقطع الصلوۃ ص ۱۱ نمبر ۷۰۲) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ عورت کے سامنے آنے سے نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی۔
(484) And the man's intention of imamate is a condition for the validity of women's following him.

Translation: (484) [2] And for the correctness of women's following, the man's intention of being imam is a condition. Explanation: The woman following the imam will be correct when the imam has explicitly intended to be the imam for the woman, and if he does not intend to be the imam for the woman, then the woman's following him is not correct. But there is another narration: if the woman stands behind, even if the imam does not intend her, following the imam is permissible.
Proof: (1) The Hanafi school's position is that the intention of the woman and the man is one, and if the woman stands alongside the man, then the man's prayer becomes invalid. Because there is a risk of the man's prayer being invalidated due to alignment (muhadhat), so intending the imamate of the woman is necessary. (2) Abu Hanifa informed us from Hammad from Ibrahim who said: If a woman prays next to a man and they are in one prayer, his prayer becomes invalid. Muhammad said: We adopt this, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa. In another athar: It only invalidates his prayer when she prays next to him and they are in one prayer, she following him or both following someone else, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa. (Kitab al-Athar of Imam Muhammad, Bab ma yaqta' al-salah, p.27, no.137, 138) This athar indicates that if the prayer is united, it becomes invalid. (3) Although this hadith is considered abrogated, it supports this. From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The woman, the donkey, and the dog invalidate the prayer, and that is prevented by something like the back of a saddle.' (Muslim, Bab qadr ma yastur al-musalli, p.209, no.1139/511; Abu Dawud, Bab ma la yaqta' al-salah, p.11, no.702) This hadith shows that the prayer breaks due to a woman passing in front.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Thamaratun Najah on the imam's intention for women followers. The ruling states: the imam must specifically intend to lead women for their following to be valid. The author first gives the ruling in Arabic, then a Urdu translation and explanation. The commentary mentions two views: the relied-upon view that intention is required, and another narration that if the woman stands behind, it is valid without intention. The proofs include an athar from Ibrahim reported by Abu Hanifa: if a woman and man pray together in one prayer, the man's prayer is invalid. Imam Muhammad says they adopt this view, which is Abu Hanifa's. Another athar confirms this. The author also cites the well-known hadith about women, donkeys, and dogs cutting the prayer, even though this hadith is considered abrogated, it supports the ruling. The underlying reason is the danger of muhadhat (alignment) which invalidates the man's prayer. The teacher should emphasize that the mufta bihi (operative position) is the requirement of intention, as Imam Muhammad adopted Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
الامامة (al-imāmah): The act of leading the prayer; the position of the imam.
الاقتداء (al-iqtidā’): Following the imam in prayer; the act of being a ma'mum.
المحاذاة (al-muḥādhaāh): Alignment; the woman standing alongside the man in prayer, which can invalidate the man's prayer according to some views.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a male imam leads Zuhr prayer and a woman follows him without his specific intention to lead her, what is the status of her prayer?
A) Valid
B) Invalid
C) Requires repetition
D) Depends on whether she stands behind

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the imam to intend leading women for their following to be valid, based on the risk of muhadhat and the athar from Ibrahim.

Imam's Heel Should Be Ahead of Follower
States ruling and proof on imam's position relative to follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended position of the imam relative to the follower, identify the evidence from the hadith of Anas, and explain the ruling level (sunnah muakkadah).

Core Idea
The imam should stand slightly ahead by the length of his heel — a strongly recommended sunnah.

In congregational prayer, the arrangement of the rows is a matter of etiquette and devotion. This lesson explains the recommended position for the imam relative to the follower, based on a hadith of Anas ibn Malik. The Hanafi school considers it a sunnah muakkadah for the imam to be slightly ahead, measured by the heel.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its level
The ruling is that the imam's heel should be ahead of the follower's heel. This is a sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended).
It is not a condition (shart) or pillar (rukn).
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
The proof is the hadith of Anas ibn Malik: the Prophet (PBUH) prayed with Anas and an orphan behind him, and Umm Sulaym behind them. This shows the imam ahead and the follower behind.
The hadith is in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Understand the indication (isharah)
The Hanafi school deduces that the imam should be slightly ahead from this practice. The indication is that the follower stands behind, so the imam is naturally forward.
This is a matter of adab (etiquette), not a binding command.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۳۸۵) [۳] اور امام کی ایڑی مقتدی سے آگے ہو۔
تشریح : امام کی شان یہ ہے کہ وہ مقتدی سے تھوڑا آگے ہو اس لئے امام کی ایڑی مقتدی سے آگے ہو تو آگے سمجھا جائے گا۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث کے اشارے سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک قال صليت اناو یتیم فی بیتنا خلف النبي وامي خلفنا ام سلیم بخاری شریف، باب المرأة وحدها تكون صفا ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۷۲۷ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب اذا کانوا ثلثہ کیف لیقومون جی ۹۷ نمبر ۶۱۲) اس حدیث میں مقتدی کو پیچھے کھڑا کیا جس سے استدلال کیا جاسکتا ہے کہ ایک مقتدی ہو تب بھی وہ تھوڑا پیچھے رہے۔
Translation: (385) [3] And the imam's heel is ahead of the follower.
Explanation: The dignity of the imam is that he be slightly ahead of the follower, therefore if the imam's heel is ahead of the follower, he will be considered ahead. Proof: (1) This can be deduced from the indication of this hadith. From Anas ibn Malik: I prayed and an orphan in our house behind the Prophet, and my mother Umm Sulaym behind us. (Bukhari, Bab al-mar'u wahdaha takunu saffan, p.188, no.727; Abu Dawud, Bab idha kanu thalathah kayfa yaqumun, p.97, no.612) In this hadith, the follower is made to stand behind, from which it can be deduced that even if there is a single follower, he should remain slightly behind.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the positioning of the imam relative to the follower. The ruling states that the imam's heel should be ahead of the follower's heel, meaning the imam stands slightly forward. The author explains that the dignity (shan) of the imam requires him to be slightly ahead. The proof is from the hadith of Anas ibn Malik: The Prophet (peace be upon him) led the prayer with Anas and an orphan behind him, and Umm Sulaym behind them. This shows that the followers stand behind the imam, even if they are few. The author uses this as an indication (isharah) that the imam should be ahead. Note that this hadith is not directly commanding the heel position but implies it. The teacher should note that this is a matter of etiquette (adab) and not a strict condition; the prayer is valid even if imam and follower are level, but it is recommended for the imam to be slightly forward.

Key Terms
العقب (al-'aqib): The heel of the foot; the back part of the foot.
المقتدي (al-muqtadī): The follower; the person praying behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended position of the imam relative to the follower according to the Hanafi school?
A) The imam should stand exactly level with the follower.
B) The imam's heel should be ahead of the follower's heel.
C) The imam should stand behind the follower.
D) There is no specific recommendation.

Key Takeaway
The imam's heel should be slightly ahead of the follower's heel; this is a sunnah muakkadah, not a condition.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Unity of Fard Prayer Between Imam and Follower
States a condition for valid congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of unity of fard in congregational prayer and determine the validity of a congregation where the imam and follower intend different obligatory prayers.

Core Idea
For a congregation to be valid, imam and follower must intend the same fard prayer.

This lesson examines a fundamental condition for the validity of congregational prayer: the imam and the follower must be performing the same obligatory prayer. The source text states this clearly and provides an example: if the imam prays Zuhr and the follower intends 'Asr, the congregation is invalid. Understanding this condition is essential for every Muslim who prays in congregation, as it ensures the unity and coherence of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
The text states that the imam should not be praying a fard different from the follower's fard. Identify the condition: there must be unity (ittihad) in the specific fard prayer being performed.
The condition applies to obligatory prayers only, not to nafl or sunnah prayers.
2
Understand the Consequence
If the condition is violated, the congregational prayer is invalid. The follower's prayer does not count as being behind the imam and must be repeated individually.
The invalidity is from the start; it does not break a valid prayer but prevents validity.
3
Apply to Scenarios
Use the example given: imam praying Zuhr, follower intending 'Asr → invalid. Then test a new scenario: imam praying Maghrib, follower intending Isha → also invalid, because the fard prayers differ.
The intention must match exactly; even if both are fard, they must be the same type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۸۷) [۵] اور امام ایسا فرض پڑھنے والا نہ ہو جو مقتدی کے فرض کے علاوہ ہو۔
تشریح : او پر حدیث میں گزرا کہ امام اور مقتدی میں اتحاد ہو اس لئے مثلا امام ظہر پڑھ رہا اور مقتدی اس کے پیچھے عصر کی نماز پڑھ رہا تو جائز نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ امام اور مقتدی کے فرض میں اتحاد چاہئے ۔ حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔
Translation: (487) [5] And the imam should not be one who prays a fard other than the follower's fard.
Explanation: It has passed in the hadith above that there should be unity between imam and follower. Therefore, for example, if the imam is praying Zuhr and the follower is praying 'Asr behind him, it is not permissible, because unity in fard is required between imam and follower. The hadith has passed.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This is a brief ruling statement: the imam and follower must be praying the same obligatory prayer. The author refers to a hadith mentioned earlier about unity (ittihad) between imam and follower. The example given: if the imam prays Zuhr and the follower prays 'Asr behind him, it is invalid because the two fard prayers are different. The text does not provide new proof but references a previous hadith (likely the hadith 'the imam is appointed to be followed'). The teacher should note that this ruling applies only when both are performing fard prayers; if one is performing nafl (supererogatory) behind an imam doing fard, it is valid in the Hanafi school (though with some conditions). The key point: the unity of the specific fard prayer (e.g., both Zuhr, both 'Asr) is required.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-farḍ): Obligatory prayer; the specific fard that one intends to perform.
الاتحاد (al-ittiḥād): Unity; the imam and follower must be performing the same type of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is it valid for a person to pray 'Asr behind an imam praying Zuhr?
A) Yes, as long as both are fard.
B) No, because the fard prayers must be the same.
C) Yes, if the follower makes a separate intention.
D) No, unless the imam knows the follower's intention.

Key Takeaway
Unity of the specific fard prayer is a necessary condition for valid congregation in the Hanafi school.
